{"date_created": 1359107395, "weight": ["73.60", "39.97", "95.61", "95.28", "19.65"], "content": "title: Funfetti Cupcake for One ,  \u00ab Sign up here for NEW exclusive & always free healthy recipes \u00bb \u00d7 Search this website Skip to primary navigation Skip to content Skip to primary sidebar Skip to footer Chocolate Covered Katie The Healthy Dessert Blog Main navigation Home About Recipe Index FAQ FAQ \u2013 Katie \u00bb Recipe Questions \u00bb Work With Me \u00bb Media & Contact \u00bb Home  \u00bb Funfetti Cupcake for One Funfetti Cupcake for One 2nd January 2012  By Chocolate Covered Katie 132 Comments Happy 2012! Did you stay up \u2018til midnight this year? I had a really low-key Sunday to make up for a crazy New Year\u2019s Eve the night before. Since our party wasn\u2019t starting until ten, Emily and I offered to babysit the two sweetest children in the universe so their parents could go out for dinner. Normally, I don\u2019t like to babysit\u2013and I can count on one hand the number of times I\u2019ve done it since high school\u2014but these girls are a joy  to watch. It\u2019s like hanging out with friends, and they love to bake and taste-test for me! The last time I babysat, we made Fairy Dust Ice Cream . Saturday, sprinkles took center stage again: We \u201cpretend\u201d celebrated New Year\u2019s at 8 o\u2019clock. We blew paper horns, drank sparkling apple cider, and the girls ate their cupcakes: Single-Lady Funfetti Cupcake (makes just one cupcake) 3 tbsp flour (30g) (See directions for flour notes) heaping 1/16th tsp salt 1tbsp applesauce, oil, pre-melted vegan butter, or a combo (Try coconut oil. I also like 13g sbl.) 1tbsp plus 1 tsp liquid (milk of choice, or water) 1/4 tsp vanilla extract 1/4 tsp baking powder 2 tsp sprinkles (or more or less, as desired) Sweetener (Try 1\u00a0tbsp sugar or 1 packet stevia. If you use liquid sweetener, cut back on the other liquid.) Directions: Preheat the oven to 330 degrees. Mix the ingredients and pour into an oiled (or sprayed) muffin pan. Smooth top of batter. Cook for 12-15ish minutes. (Alternatively, you can cook this in a microwave.) See the following for Calories and Nutrition Facts . Notes on flour: I especially like the single-lady cupcakes with spelt flour. But you can use white flour, whole-wheat pastry, or even Arrowhead Mills gluten-free. (Also, if you\u2019ve never done fat-free baking: subbing all the oil in a recipe for applesauce will give you a gummier result. Still yummy, but much denser than your traditional cupcake with oil.) Questions of the Day: This New Year\u2019s Eve, did you\u2026 Stay up until midnight? Watch the ball drop in Times Square? Eat any lucky foods, such as lentils or greens? Or sprinkles. They\u2019re lucky, right? For more sprinkles: Here\u2019s a link to My Funfetti Recipes . I did end up making a dessert for the New Year\u2019s Eve party as well. That recipe will be tomorrow\u2019s post\u2026 Hope you like cookie dough! \ud83d\ude42 No ratings yet. {"date_created": 1432296344, "weight": ["26.67", "15.85", "17.44", "51.44", "69.00"], "content": "title: Double Chocolate Peanut Butter Mug Cookie - Crazy for Crust ,  Home About FAQ Contact Cookbooks work with me Recipes by Category Bread Breakfast brownies and bars Cake Candy Cookies Drinks Savory No Bake Holidays More \u00bb by Ingredient chocolate peanut butter caramel apple pumpkin More \u00bb Recipe Index All Recipes Travel About Locations Central California Half Moon Bay Napa San Francisco Southern USA More Adults Business Family Food Lunch Break Sights Tips Lifestyle Home Printables School Days Party Birthday Kids\u2019 Parties Sports Crumbs Slice of Life Blogging Things Extras Subscribe Never miss a recipe! Get new posts via email: Double Chocolate Peanut Butter Mug Cookie January 6, 2014 Recipes Pin 26K Share 886 Tweet Stumble Yum 105 Email Perfect for when you just want one dessert not three dozen, this Double Chocolate Peanut Butter Mug Cookie  will satisfy your sweet tooth and not ruin your diet (and the peanut butter is optional!) {Hahahahaha. I just said peanut butter optional. #wordsineverthoughtiwouldsay} Hi everyone! You may not know it but I\u2019ve been kiiiiind of ignoring this space for the last two weeks. All my posts through yesterday were scheduled before Christmas. I wish I could say I\u2019ve just been relaxing on the couch for the past two weeks, soaking up books and movies, but alas. I\u2019ve been arm deep in batter and cheesecake and cookies. Such is life\u2026for another month or so. It\u2019ll be worth it in the end. Anyway. the other day I asked on Facebook\u00a0 \u00a0if I should post a mug cookie or a regular cookie recipe today. And overwhelmingly the answer was MUG! And I\u2019m super glad too, because the cookie recipe is fabulous (coming later this week) but this mug cookie is WOW. It\u2019s a cookie. For one. In a mug. It\u2019s a chocolate cookie. With mini chocolate chips. And peanut butter. In a mug. Single-serve. For one. If you\u2019re not like me and don\u2019t have two identical (but for the failed crust on one) cheesecake bars, a batch of donuts, and three dozen cookies on their counter, and you want something sweet but not a whole batch , this recipe is for you. I adapted an adaption of this chocolate cookie recipe  to make this cookie. This is where my nerdy math background (summa cum laude in mathematics, thankyouverymuch, although I laugh when I think about it because I\u2019m so not even close to that level anymore, if I even was) comes in handy. I can convert fractions of cups into tablespoons and teaspoons and divide by 12 or 36 or whatever. It\u2019s actually quite simple\u2026which I know just made about 3/4 of you roll your eyes. The tricky part is the egg. How do you twelfth an egg? You don\u2019t. You adjust other things so that you can use 1 yolk. It\u2019s just how it is. The beauty of this recipe is that you can make it egg-free  by substituting milk or water (1 tablespoon) for the egg yolk. It won\u2019t rise as much or be as rich, but it\u2019ll still be good. The chocolate and richness of this cookie make it taste like a brownie. A rich fudgy brownie that\u2019s actually a cookie that\u2019s been 36th\u2019d. The peanut butter is just because I\u2019m\u2026me. Everything is better with peanut butter, especially chocolate and fudgy cookies. I just added a dollop of Super Chunk Skippy  Naturals (my favorite brand). You can totally leave it off, or use Nutella or Biscoff or any other nut butter or spread. It whisks up in a few minutes and cooks in 30 seconds. Perfect when you need chocolate NOW but got rid of it all because it\u2019s January. It\u2019s almost too easy. I\u2019m sorry? Print Recipe Did you make this recipe? Leave a review \u00bb Double Chocolate Peanut Butter Mug Cookie Ingredients: 1 tablespoon butter (you can substitute butter spread) 1 tablespoon brown sugar 1 teaspoon granulated sugar 3 drops pure vanilla extract 1/8 teaspoon baking powder 1 egg yolk (or 1 tablespoon water or milk, but it's won't be as high or as rich) 2 teaspoons cocoa powder 1 tablespoon flour 1 tablespoon mini chocolate chips 1 tablespoon peanut butter (creamy or chunky), optional (also try Nutella, Biscoff, or any other spread) Directions: Place butter in an 8-ounce coffee mug (or bigger, but it doesn\u2019t grow much). Melt in the microwave, about 20 seconds. Stir in sugars, vanilla, and baking powder. Stir in egg yolk, coca, and flour. Stir in chocolate chips. Place peanut butter in the center and press it down slightly into the batter. Heat in the microwave for 30 seconds. Let cool slightly before eating. All images and text \u00a9 Dorothy Kern for  . Please do not use my images without prior permission. (And it totally helps confused customers on the baking aisles who need to know how many teaspoons are in a tablespoon and how many tablespoons are in a cup.) I ran into the problem of dividing eggs a few years ago when trying to halve a cake recipe with 3 eggs. I started using an egg substitute called Ener-G (very popular in vegan baking!). It\u2019s a shelf-stable powder (lasts for months, if not years!), and 1 1/2 tsp Ener-G + 2 tbsp warm water = 1 egg. Much easier to divide that kind of egg by 12! \ud83d\ude09 \u2014 Dorothy Kern January 6, 2014 @ 7:42 pm Reply Sweet! I need to find that. For birthdays my kids LOVE giant cookie cakes or skillet brownies. \u00a0I will on occasion make cupcakes  at Stella\u2019s request, but even that doesn\u2019t happen very often. My cake pans pretty much just collect dust in the back of my cupboards. But, Easter is nearly here, and in case you have not noticed, carrot cake is everywhere. So what\u2019s a girl to do when she wants carrot cake? really Make it single serving, and healthier, that\u2019s what, and it\u2019s ready in less than 5 minutes, so I can have it whenever  I want. Print Single Serving Carrot Cake {in a mug} Ingredients 1/4 cup flour 1 Tbsp sugar 1/2 tsp cinnamon 1/4 tsp nutmeg 1/2 tsp baking powder dash of salt 1 Tbsp coconut oil {melted} 1 Tbsp milk 1/2 tsp vanilla 1 carrot grated Instructions in a microwave cup, combine all of the dry ingredients stir in the coconut oil, milk, and vanilla finally, stir in the grated carrot microwave on high  about 90 seconds {check after 1 minute} top with vanilla yogurt and pecan {optional} 3.1 http://www.wellfloured.com/single-serving-carrot-cake-mug/ Like for breakfast Enjoy! more treats in mugs blueberry muffin in a mug red velvet hot cocoa cake 40 Comments \u00bb You May Also Like: Mini Flourless Chocolate Cakes blueberry muffin cake molasses pound cake 40 comments \u2014 Dorothy @ Crazy for Crust April 7, 2014 @ 6:51 pm Reply I am SO in love with this Heather! {"date_created": 969344096, "weight": ["27.82", "47.68", "48.67", "14.65", "38.82"], "content": "title: Single Serving Chocolate Chip Cupcake - The Glowing Fridge ,  Skip to primary navigation Skip to content Skip to primary sidebar Skip to footer Main navigation Home Recipes Breakfast Smoothies and Juices Drinks Salads Main Dish Glow Bowls Soup Sides Sauces, Dressings and Dips Snacks Sweets Mocktails & Cocktails 5-Day Cleanse Vegan Starter Guide Beauty Lifestyle The Glow Down Wellness & Lifestyle What I Ate Why Vegan? About About Me My Vegan Story Contact Videos Shop eBooks The Glowing Fridge Plant Based Vegan Lifestyle and Recipe Blog 01/02/2015 Chocolate Single Serving Chocolate Chip Cupcake 58 350 0 WordPress tells me this is my 100th post\u2026\u00a0I think that calls for a mini magical celebration. Weeee! Since we celebrate with sweets over here, this is a Single Serving Chocolate Chip Cupcake just for you \u2013 because sometimes all you need is 1 cupcake \u2013 not 12. And let\u2019s be real, spring break is like, right around the corner. While I would love to eat 12 of these cutie cupcakes, I should probably stick to one.. I\u2019m also trying something new in January! I\u2019m going oil-free for the month with Lindsay from The Planted Palate .\u00a0We decided to team up so we can help each other out. Please join us! I\u2019ll be sharing oil-free yumminess for the entire month. I\u2019m not saying I will go oil-free forever but I want to give it a shot and see if I honestly miss it or if it\u2019s all in my head. There\u2019s no such thing as \u201chealthy oils\u201d and I want to challenge myself to come up with oil-free recipes that are mouthwatering, enticing and plant based. Check out this post  to read more about oils, what to replace them with and why cutting back on them is beneficial for your health. So this cupcake is vegan, gluten-free, nut-free, oil-free and for the hippies. Just kidding! (about the hippies part) It\u2019s actually the yummiest and most adorable cupcake I\u2019ve ever made. Plus you can\u2019t go wrong with coconut cream frosting. So who wants to join us and go oil-free in January?! I\u2019ve significantly cut back on cooking with oil the past couple months and I\u2019m finding it totally unnecessary. I used to think cooking with oil was for flavor \u2013 that is so not the case! You will not miss all those empty calories \u2013 especially in this cupcake. Instead of oil, I used applesauce which I do quite often in baking. I hope you enjoy! Chocolate Chip Cupcake For One 2015-01-02 14:03:27 Serves 1 Write a review Save Recipe Print Prep Time 5 min Cook Time 15 min Total Time 20 min Prep Time 5 min Cook Time 15 min Total Time 20 min Ingredients 3 tablespoons gluten-free all-purpose flour (buckwheat, millet, etc. I also used spelt flour) 1 tablespoon coconut sugar (or raw cane sugar) 1/4 teaspoon baking powder tiny pinch of fine grain sea salt 1 tablespoon + 1 teaspoon unsweetened almond milk 1 tablespoon applesauce 1/2 tablespoon dairy-free chocolate chips (like the Enjoy Life brand) Coconut Cream Frosting 2 tablespoons coconut cream (*1 can full-fat coconut milk, refrigerated overnight) 1/4 teaspoon coconut sugar Instructions Preheat oven to 330 degrees F. Line a cupcake tin with one cupcake liner. In a small bowl, combine flour, sugar, baking powder and salt. Mix well. Add in the almond milk, applesauce and chocolate chips. Mix until well combined. Pour mixture into the cupcake liner and bake for 14-15 minutes or until a toothpick comes out clean. To make Coconut Cream Open a can of full-fat coconut milk that has been refrigerated overnight. Scoop out 2 tablespoons of the cream from the top of the can (it has separated from the water) and place in a small bowl. Add coconut sugar and whisk until creamy. Frost your cupcake after it has cooled. Enjoy! Notes Save the remaining coconut cream and water to use in a smoothie or soup! Adapted from Chocolate Covered Katie Adapted from Chocolate Covered Katie The Glowing Fridge http://www.theglowingfridge.com/ Thank you for following TGF on this health journey and supporting a plant based way of life. If you want to participate this month, use the hashtag #oilfreejanuary  on social media. Happy weekend and HAPPY 2015!! By adding your email you agree to get updates about Spoon University Healthier Craving a pumpkin dessert late at night? Since no one has time to make a pumpkin pie in the middle of the week, we are grateful that someone out there invented baking dishes and mugs. You can make your own healthy, vegan \u00a0pumpkin cake with just a microwave in your very own kitchen. This recipe makes just enough for one hungry person or 2 people who like to share. If it was up to me though, I would eat it all myself. Easy Prep Time:\u00a0 5 minutes Cook Time:\u00a0 1 minute 6 minutes Total Time: Servings:\u00a0 1 Ingredients: 2 tablespoon all purpose flour 1/8 teaspoon baking powder 3/4 tablespoon sugar 1 tablespoon pumpkin puree 2 tablespoon milk 1/2 tablespoon vegetable oil 1/8 teaspoon cinnamon Photo by Emily Hu Directions: 1. Combine all ingredients in a ramekin dish or mug. Photo by Emily Hu 2. Mix well until combined smoothly. Photo by Emily Hu 3. Cook in microwave for 1 minute. The top of the cake should be dry; if not, microwave for a few more seconds. Let cake cool a few minutes before eating. {"date_created": 1059915962, "weight": ["51.04", "51.37", "76.93", "16.70", "27.62"], "content": "title: Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe - The Chic Life ,  Skip links Skip to primary navigation Skip to content Skip to primary sidebar Skip to footer Main navigation Home About Bailey Plateware Eat in Month Challenge Blogroll Recipes 30 Minutes or Less Breakfast Smoothies Eggs and Savories Oatmeal and Grains Muffins and Breads Dinner Chicken and Turkey Beef and Meat Soup Side Dish Dessert Cakes and Cupcakes Cookies and Bars Pies and Tarts Other Baked Goods No Bake Sweets Drink Popular Vegetarian Vegan Recipes by Photo Planner How to Decorate Your Planner Planner Decoration Ideas Planner Decoration Supplies Planner Blog Posts Fitness Zumba Zumba Convention ZinCon FAQ Theme Class Ideas Fitness Blog Posts Contact Resources The Chic Life Make every day chic 3 May 15, 2012 Not So Sweet Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe Here\u2019s a fun project to try this strawberry season\u2026a Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe! Does this look familiar ? From the photo, we appear  to have something I\u2019ve blogged about before \u2013 Farm-Fresh Strawberry Shortcakes with Amaretto-Spiked Whipped Cream  ( click for recipe ). It looks like a rich shortcake with sugar-sweetened strawberries and fluffy, potentially-spiked, whipped cream, right? As it turns out, looks can definitely be deceiving\u2026 Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe What we actually have here is a strawberry shortcake made-over for breakfast. For this Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe, I added one of my favorite breakfast ingredients \u2013 oats. I also used a whole grain flour (spelt), cut the sugar by not macerating the strawberries in sugar, and found a fabulous, breakfast-worthy substitute for the whipped cream \u2013 yogurt. I\u2019m not going to promise you that this is healthy, but it is more breakfast-friendly. Would a chocolate croissant have more butter and sugar? I don\u2019t really know, and I don\u2019t really care. But, anywho, you could probably use this version as another Not So Sweet  dessert with even less sugar than the original . Just tell them it\u2019s good for you because of the probiotics. Yeaaaaaa\u2026 Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One {Recipe} Print Prep time 5 mins Cook time 15 mins Total time 20 mins Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One I took my dessert strawberry shortcake recipe and switched up the ingredients to make it more breakfast-friendly. I used a whole grain flour, added oats, skipped macerating the strawberries, and substituted yogurt for the whipped cream. You could probably make this even healthier by substituting a good oil (maybe coconut?) for the butter (and please report back if you do). Oh, and I took almost all of the sugar out of this baby, so if you like your breakfast sweeter, by all means, add your preferred sweetener, to taste. *Vegetarian, Vegan Options Listed* Author: Diana of thechiclife.com Serves: 1 Ingredients \u00bc cup spelt flour (or flour of choice) 2 tablespoons oats 2 teaspoons sugar \u00bc teaspoon baking powder \u215b teaspoon salt 1 tablespoon butter, cold (or sub vegan substitute, like Earth Balance) 3 tablespoons milk (or vegan non-dairy milk) 3-4 strawberries, tops removed, sliced 1 small container vanilla, Greek yogurt (or yogurt of choice or vegan yogurt, like a coconut-milk-based option) - or sub plain yogurt and add sweetener of choice, to taste Instructions Pre-heat oven to 400 degrees F. Prepare a small baking sheet with parchment paper. Combine flour, oats, sugar, baking powder, and salt in a medium-sized bowl. Whisk (or use a fork) to evenly combine. Use a pastry cutter or fork to cut butter into the dry ingredients until the butter is in small bits (about the size of rice grains or pop rocks...yea, I said pop rocks). Gently stir in the milk/non-dairy milk until just combined (careful to not over-mix, but do ensure all flour combined into dough). Form dough into a ball-shape and place on the prepared baking sheet. Bake for 15-18 minutes, until golden brown on top and cooked through (if a toothpick inserted in the center comes out clean). Allow to cool to room temperature. Cut shortcake in half. Top bottom half of shortcake with strawberries. Stir yogurt to desired texture and spoon as much as you'd like (I used about half the container) over the strawberries. Top yogurt with top half of shortcake and enjoy. 3.4.3177 More Delicious Baked Recipes Farm-Fresh Strawberry Shortcakes with Amaretto-Spiked Whipped Cream Green Monster Muffins  (or click here for the vegan version ) Individual Peach Blueberry Breakfast Crisp Dessert for breakfast? You betcha. *** Click here to get free updates  (even delivered to your email inbox). And we\u2019ve been having some great conversation over on my Facebook page . Click here to take a look and like my page . Hope you enjoy this Mini Breakfast Strawberry Shortcake for One Recipe. {"date_created": 1089667703, "weight": ["78.58", "29.69", "52.56", "75.93", "45.35"], "content": "title: Cinnamon Streusel Coffee Cake for One (in a Jar) ,  Home About Start Somewhere: A Postpartum Health Series This IS My Real Job 5 Things I\u2019ve Learned\u2026 Contact Speaking Blog Love What I Love About\u2026 Bloglovin Facebook Google+ Instagram Pinterest RSS Twitter YouTube Heather's Dish Recipes Breakfast Lunch/Dinner Dessert Snacks, Soups, Sides Beautycounter Travel Our Family Fashion The Dish Heather's Dish Cinnamon Streusel Coffee Cake for One (in a Jar) Share 1 Pin 40 Tweet Shares  41 I\u2019ve figured it out. I\u2019ve figured out how to do portion control for sweets. I\u2019m hesitant to share, but I think it\u2019s important so here goes. The secret\u2026 to perfect portion control\u2026 is\u2026 To make it a pain in the ass to make another one. Confused?\u00a0 Let me explain. When it comes to coffee cake, specifically the kind with a lovely streusel topping, I have almost zero self control.\u00a0 It\u2019s just so stinking delicious and I think that deep down I just really want to eat the entire thing in one sitting, so I do and then blame it on the streusel.\u00a0 Or the fact that I did 100 lunges uphill  yesterday on our walk and can now no longer feel my legs.\u00a0 Yeah, that wasn\u2019t a smart move. Oops. But I discovered the other day that if I make one tiny little cake that it just becomes too much for me to actually make two of them, so I eat the one and only wish for a second rather than eating it.\u00a0 It\u2019s genius!\u00a0 Not to mention completely and totally delicious and completely and totally worth it to double, triple, or quadruple the recipe and eat it all on the spot  save some for later.\u00a0 So I guess I should say:\u00a0 forget what I said earlier about this being a pain to make.\u00a0 That\u2019s just me whining on account of my legs, but it\u2019s nothing a little coffee cake can\u2019t cure. CINNAMON STREUSEL COFFEE CAKE FOR ONE (IN A JAR) For the cake: 2 Tbsp sugar 2 Tbsp plain yogurt 1 egg white 2 1/2 Tbsp flour 1/8 tsp baking powder 1/8 tsp salt 1/4 tsp vanilla For the streusel: 2 Tbsp butter, cut into small cubes 2 Tbsp brown sugar 1 Tbsp flour 1/2 tsp cinnamon Preheat your oven to 350 and spray the inside of an 8 oz. wide-mouth mason jar with nonstick spray (if you don\u2019t have a jar you can certainly use an oven-safe ramekin, but make sure you want it as it will likely bake faster).\u00a0 Whisk together the sugar, yogurt egg white and vanilla until smooth.\u00a0 Fold in the flour, baking powder and salt until everything is combined.\u00a0 For the streusel mix together the cubed butter pieces, brown sugar, cinnamon and flour and using your fingers work the butter into the dry ingredients until a fine crumb forms.\u00a0 Pour half of the batter into the bottom of the jar, top with 1/3 of the streusel mixture, top with the remaining batter and then top the entire thing off with the remaining streusel mixture.\u00a0 Place on a baking sheet lined with foil and bake at 350 for 20-25 minutes or until a toothpick inserted comes out clean.\u00a0 Let cool before eating, and be careful\u2026the jar will be hot!\u00a0 I topped mine with a little cream cheese frosting  that I melted slightly. Pain in the ass my ass \ud83d\ude42 Share 1 Pin 40 Tweet Shares  41 49 Comments Subscribe for the latest. email address \u00ab Blog Love:  Crock Pot Kung Pao Chicken Week 8:  The Cutest \u00bb Leave a Reply  \t\t\t \t\t\t\tYou have to agree to the comment policy. {"date_created": 1352047783, "weight": ["23.90", "56.20", "18.43", "63.02", "47.74"], "content": "title: 10 Minute Microwave Cheesecake Mug Cake - Kirbie&#039;s Cravings ,  Home About About Us Contact Press Work with me! Recipes Full Recipe Index 30 Minute Meals 4 Ingredients or Less Appetizers/Side Dishes Asian dishes Bacon Breakfast foods Cakes Cauliflower Cookies Drinks Gluten Free Main dishes Mug cakes Nutella Dining Restaurant Index by City Restaurant Index by Cuisine Best of San Diego On the Side Personal Photography Equipment Product Reviews Travel October 30, 2013 10 Minute Microwave Cheesecake Mug Cake by Kirbie Pin 17K Share 517 Tweet Yum 4K Email Ten minutes is all the time you\u2019ll need to prep and cook this individual serving of cheesecake. Look how pretty it is! I don\u2019t usually ever have an entire cheesecake in the house and I rarely make it. My brothers and Mr. K used to always ask for it and then it was like pulling teeth to get them to finish it once I did. And I can never eat more than one slice. MY LATEST VIDEOS That is why this one serving treat is so perfect. The texture isn\u2019t exact. It\u2019s close, but the microwave version doesn\u2019t come out as creamy as the baked version. I tried a few attempts but haven\u2019t gotten it to be exactly like the baked version yet. I\u2019ll keep trying. But it tastes like cheesecake and it was delicious. The one thing is, just like a regular baked cheesecake, you need to let this cool. I\u2019m so used to eating a mug cake right after it comes out of the microwave, but this is cheese and when cheese is warm, well, it doesn\u2019t really taste like cheesecake. It tastes like warm, sweetened cheese, and it\u2019s a little oily. So definitely give this time to cool in the fridge. I let mine cool for an hour. You can check out my entire mug cake recipe collection . here Hot Off the Press! This recipe, along with many brand new  recipes are in my new cookbook . Microwave Cheesecake Mug Cake Print Recipe Ingredients: for the cheesecake: 4 tbsp light cream cheese (you can also use cream cheese spread which actually is much easier to mix, though the final cake has looser layers) 2 tbsp plain Greek yogurt (or sour cream) 2 1/2 tbsp granulated sugar (less if you are using a sweetened flavored cheese spread) 1 egg 1/4 tsp vanilla for the crust: 4 tbsp graham cracker crumbs (place through food processor to get fine crumbs. 4 tbsp is about 1 sheet of graham cracker) 1 tbsp melted butter Directions: 1. Grease the inside of a microwave-safe mug (both interior sides and bottom). Add graham cracker crumbs and melted butter and mix until butter is incorporated. Press down with your hands so the graham cracker crumbs form a crust at bottom of mug. 2. In a small bowl, whisk egg. Then add cream cheese, yogurt, sugar and vanilla. Using a small whisk, mix until batter is smooth. If you are using cream cheese and not spread, there may remain lumps of cream cheese. If that is the case, use a bigger whisk, which should help you break up all the lumps. Pour batter into mug. 3. Cover top of mug with a paper towel or napkin and microwave for 1 minute. Mug cake should be mostly cooked except center. Pause to check on it, then microwave for another 20 seconds. Stop again, and microwave for another 20 seconds. Then microwave for one final round of 20 seconds. Cake should be completely cooked. You don't want to microwave the entire amount at once because the batter may overheat and start popping and exploding in the microwave. 4. If you have greased your mug, the cheesecake should have pulled away from the sides of the mug. Gently slide cheesecake out of the mug. I let it come out upside down onto a big spatula and then flipped it back over onto a plate. Let cool cake at room temperature for a few minutes. When cake is no longer too hot to touch, place in fridge to cool and set for at least 1 hour. All images and content are \u00a9 Kirbie's Cravings. Did you make this recipe? Welcome to my baking adventures. July 17, 2012 Chocolate Chip Cookie Dough Mug Cake Chocolate Chip Cookie Dough Mug Cake-perfect when you just want a little something sweet! Mug Cakes! It\u2019s summertime, It\u2019s hot, too hot to have the oven on baking a cake. I remember when microwaves first came out. My grandparents were the first ones to get one. We got one about 3-4 years later. It was their old one, they got a newer, better model. My mom went to town cooking everything she could in it. They came out with special baking dishes and recipe books to\u00a0encourage\u00a0you to cook in this new machine. She even tried to bake cakes a few times but they always came out rubbery and the taste was off. I hated those cakes. Things have come a long way since then. I still\u00a0prefer\u00a0to bake a cake in the oven. The smell of it baking, the crisp outer texture it takes on, the anticipation while it bakes. These just seem right to me. So when you make a microwave mug cake, remember. the baking aroma will only last a minute. This little cake was surprisingly good and with a scoop of ice cream, perfect for a hot summer day treat! Connect with Chocolate Chocolate and More! | Facebook | Twitter Google+ Pinterest \u00a0| instagram Save your favorite recipes to your personal recipe box \u00a0with the button on all my recipes! Create a Meal Plan \u00a0with your \u201cfavorite\u201d \u00a0recipes and the ingredients will automatically be added to your own Grocery List ! Print Chocolate Chip Cookie Dough Mug Cake Ingredients 1 egg 3 tablespoons Brown Sugar 1/3 cup flour 1 tablespoon softened butter 1/4 teaspoon vanilla 3-4 tablespoons mini chocolate chips Instructions Mix together with a spoon all ingredients except chips together with a spoon till completely combined. Stir in chips. Spoon into 2 regular mugs or one large mug. This cake won't rise too much while baking. Microwave on high 1 1/2 minutes, just until top has set. Add a scoop of ice cream and eat while still warm. While this recipe uses gluten free flour mix (instead of a whole grain), it doesn\u2019t have any refined sugars! It really is a Fit Foodie Favorite. On my agenda for this weekend is 1. Single Serve Banana Cake \u2605 \u2605 \u2605 \u2605 4  from 1  reviews Print Recipe Prep Time: 5 mins Cook Time: 18 mins Total Time: 23 minutes Yield: 1 Ingredients -3 tablespoons gluten free flour -3 tablespoons unsweetened Silk almond milk -3 inches of mashed banana or roughly 1-2 tablespoons mashed banana -1/2 tablespoon butter, melted (to make dairy free, omit and use coconut oil) -1/4 teaspoon vanilla -pinch of salt -1/4 teaspoon baking powder -1 tablespoon Dark Chocolate Chips (optional) Instructions Preheat oven to 330F and spray ramekin with nonstick cooking spray. Mix all ingredients together in a small bowl and bake for 16-18 minutes. Facebook 0 Twitter Pinterest 6 Google+ 0 Yummly 0 Email 6 Hashtag with us! {"date_created": 1408957316, "weight": ["23.00", "60.70", "33.45", "90.68", "63.52"], "content": "title: single-serving deep dish chocolate chip cookie [vegan + gluten-free] \u2014 Edible Perspective ,  single-serving deep dish chocolate chip cookie [vegan + gluten-free] \u2014 Edible Perspective Edible Perspective home About Recipes all recipes breakfast main course dessert drink side topping by ingredient Photography 101 Portfolio Cookbook contact etc links home / About / Recipes / all recipes breakfast main course dessert drink side topping by ingredient Photography 101 / Portfolio / Cookbook / contact / etc / links home home / About / Recipes / all recipes breakfast main course dessert drink side topping by ingredient Photography 101 / Portfolio / Cookbook / contact / etc / links May 22, 2013 single-serving deep dish chocolate chip cookie [vegan + gluten-free] May 22, 2013 / Ashley | edible perspective So, I know yesterday's single-serving muffins were pretty cool and all, but ummm, this recipe is slightly cooler. And let me start out by saying that I am super skeptical of gluten-free cookies. \u00a0Skeptical in buying them at the store and nervous to make them on my own. \u00a0I've come up with a few recipes  that have more than satisfied my cookie cravings but there is a specific texture I still had yet to create or find. \u00a0The chewy, gooey, sticky oatmeal chocolate chip cookie texture. This recipe solves that problem. The oatmeal cookie of my dreams. \u00a0The best gluten-free cookie I've ever eaten. \u00a0Not to mention vegan, single-serving, and can be made in 1 bowl with 1 fork using minimal ingredients in about 3 minutes. \u00a0The most non-fuss cookie ever. If I had the choice between a regular chocolate chip cookie and an oatmeal chocolate chip cookie I will pick the oatmeal cookie 100% of the time. \u00a0Rolled oats add such a nutty delicious flavor and an addictingly chewy texture you just can't get when using flour alone. The best part about this recipe is that you can bake it exactly to your liking. \u00a0Since there is no egg it doesn't matter how \"done\" it ends up. \u00a0Underbake it, overbake it, eat the raw dough for all I care! \u00a0Whatever you want! My cookie texture of choice has a slightly crispy edge with a doughy, tacky center. \u00a0Not tacky like socks with sandals but tacky like sticky and chewy. \u00a0I could eat these all day for the texture alone! \u00a0And trust me this didn't come after one lucky try. \u00a0This recipe was not an accident. \u00a0I made at least 7 trials playing with very small ratios of flour, oats, oil, sugar, etc. until it was just perfect. Well, perfect for me, anyway. \u00a0But hopefully you like it as well. \u00a0This cookie is the real deal. Or maybe it's been so long since I've had a real \u00a0cookie that my brain has been a skewed vision of what a real \u00a0cookie is. Or not. Print this! inspired by: deep-dish whole wheat vegan chocolate chip cookie Single-Serving Deep Dish Chocolate Chip Cookie gluten-free, vegan // yields 1 serving 2 teaspoons unrefined coconut oil, softened not melted 2 teaspoons brown rice syrup 1 1/2 teaspoons muscovado \u00a0sugar, or [vegan] light brown sugar 1/4 teaspoon vanilla bean paste, or vanilla extract 1/8 teaspoon baking powder 3 tablespoons gluten-free rolled oats 1 tablespoon gluten-free oat flour 1 tablespoon almond meal 1-1 1/2 tablespoons dark [vegan] chocolate chips pinch of flaked sea salt, to top Preheat your oven to 350* F and take out a 3 or 4-inch ramekin dish. In a small bowl mash the coconut oil, brown rice syrup, muscovado sugar, vanilla, and baking powder together until fully combined + creamy. Do not  use melted coconut oil. Add the oats, oat flour, and almond meal, then mash with a fork until a dough forms that is sticky and holds together. ~30 seconds Mix in the chocolate chips. Press firmly into the ramekin dish then top with a small pinch of flaked sea salt and bake for 11-13 minutes [for a 4-inch ramekin] or less/more depending on your texture preference. \u00a0For a 3-inch ramekin bake for 15-17 minutes. Remove from the oven and let cool for at least 7-10 minutes. \u00a0The cookie will firm up and become chewier as it cools. Serve slightly warm or fully cooled. \u00a0The cookie will stay chewy when fully cooled. notes/substitution:\u00a0 \u00a0The brown rice syrup helps create a chewy texture but maple syrup will also work. \u00a0For making 3 cookies instead of the cookie pie see directions below. Don't feel like smashing the dough into a ramekin dish? \u00a0Roll 3 balls of dough, place them on a cookie sheet 2-inches apart, flatten them, and bake for about 7-9 minutes [at 350*]. \u00a0Let them cool for 5 minutes then transfer to a cooling rack. \u00a0The cookies will firm up as they cool and stay chewy once fully cooled. slightly And then there's the option of serving the cookie pie a la mode. \u00a0The ice cream cools the warm cookie making it even chewier, while at the same time melting into ice cream soup. \u00a0My two favorite things together at last. And here is the whopping sinkful of dishes you'll have to clean when you're all done. Why aren't you in the kitchen yet? {"date_created": 1309088224, "weight": ["22.45", "74.13", "96.95", "35.39", "77.90"], "content": "title: My Happy Place: XXL dark chocolate & sea salt brownie cookie ,  Pages Home About Contact Recipe Index Reads FAQ's 10.03.2013 XXL dark chocolate & sea salt brownie cookie So I'm kinda on this chocolate kick lately\u2026 Exceeeeept when am I not on a chocolate kick?\u00a0Hi, my name is Sophie and I am addicted to Lindt 70% cocoa dark chocolate. {Hiiiii, Sooooophiieeeee.}\u00a0No but really. This is getting out of hand. Looking back, I just realized there hasn't been a day in the last- oh, I don't know- EVER, that I haven't had chocolate in some way shape or form. It's a crazy love for the stuff. A yearning. A desire as strong as Channing Tatum's abs. A BURNING PASSION IN MY SOOOOOUL. I'll stop. I've come to the mature decision to feed this obsession in a good, healthy way. Although  if you ask me, chocolate is pretty healthy in and of itself. It's just probably not very good if you go and eat the whole bar of chocolate, batch of brownies, pint of ice cream\u2026 You get my gist.\u00a0I'll admit.\u00a0I basically eat chocolate in every single way possible.\u00a0In my oatmeal? Dunnniiitttt. Definitely not a bad idea, if you're wondering. Smoothies? Check. Healthy brownies? Shooosh yahhhh. Eaten the whole dang pan, in fact! But let's not go there. AND NOW. COOKIES. Actually, cookiEEEEE. Just for you and your pretty little chocolate loving face. This cookie is kind of sort of a freaking SUCCCCESSSS. I've tried making a healthy single serving cookie before and oh my gross, you guys. So did not work. That experience kind of scarred me for life and I was hesitant about trying out a new recipe. Thank heavens I did though. I basically saved all of humanity with this cookie. {things get baaaaad if I don't satisfy my cravings fast.} This cookie is going to blow your mind. It's soft and chewy AND CHOCOLATEY. So much chocolate. So much happiness. GET EXCITED. The cookie itself is like a little hunk 'a fudgalicious brownie. And if that couldn't get any better, I pressed some of my beloved 70% on the top. And if THAT couldn't get any better\u2026 Sea salt. This is just pure chocolatey, fudgey greatness made JUST for you in a matter of minutes. It's actually healthy too. I know, weird huh? WHOOODA THUUUUNKED IT? It's dairy-free, gluten-free, and processed sugar free. Which MEANS. You can eat it for breakfast. With a cup of hot coffee? Oh my gosh, that is like. Heaven. Like suddenly, all is right in the world while you dip your fudgey cookie in a ginormous mug of coffee. No more werrrrrrds. \u2026\u2026 Except I do have a few more. My sincerest apologies. You know that song \"Give Me Love\" by Ed Sheeran? I am making a parody\u2026 Caaaaaalled. {drumroll please.} \"Give Me Fudge\".\u00a0Give me FUUUUUUUUHHUUUUDGE\u2026 Hmmmm myyy myyyuhhhh hmmm myyyyyy myuuhhh. Give me fuuuuuuudgeeeeee.\u00a0I sure hope you've heard that song before because otherwise, you're totally thinking I'm a fool right now. And you would be correct. Ok, thanks for listening! Now go make yerrrsehhhlf a cookie. XXL dark chocolate & sea salt brownie cookie 1 egg 1 1/2 tbsp. coconut oil 1 tbsp. nut butter {I used peanut butter. duh.} dash of vanilla 2 tbsp. pure maple syrup 1/4 c. gluten-free flour 2 tbsp. unsweetened cocoa powder 1/2 tsp. baking powder pinch of sea salt 1 square 70% cocoa dark chocolate, roughly chopped Preheat oven to 350\u00baF and line a baking sheet with parchment paper. In a small bowl, combine egg, coconut oil, nut butter, vanilla, and maple syrup. Add flour, cocoa powder, baking powder, and sea salt. Transfer to prepared baking sheet and form into a disk. Press dark chocolate chunks onto the top of the cookie and sprinkle with sea salt. Bake for 10-15 minutes. Posted by Sophie at 4:24:00 AM Email This BlogThis! Single-Serve Snickerdoodle Cookies by Work it Mom Staff \t\t\t\t\t\t\u00a0|\u00a0 \t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t \t\t\t\t\t26640 views\t\t\t\t\t\u00a0| 0 comments  \t\t\t\t\t\u00a0| Rate this now! Follow @Work_It_Mom Baking for one or just want a single treat for yourself that you don\u2019t have to share? This recipe for single-serve snickerdoodle cookies is perfect for just that! Ingredients : 2 tablespoons sugar, divided 1 tsp cinnamon, divided Heaping 1/4 cup flour Pinch of salt 1/8 tsp cream of tartar 1/4 tsp vanilla 1 tsp melted butter 1 tablespoon milk Directions : Heat the oven to 350 and line a cookie sheet with parchment paper. In a small bowl combine 1 teaspoon sugar and 1/2 teaspoon cinnamon. Set aside. In another bowl combine the flour, baking soda, salt, tartar, remaining sugar and cinnamon. Mix together. Add in the butter, milk and extract and mix again. Roll the dough into a boll and then roll that in the cinnamon sugar mixture, so the outside it coated with cinnamon sugar. Transfer to the baking sheet and press down into the shape of a cookie. Cook for 12-15 minutes or until it starts to golden slightly. {"date_created": 1287749818, "weight": ["15.58", "12.21", "23.47", "66.06", "39.94"], "content": "title: Gluten-Free &amp; Egg-Free &ldquo;Cookie Dough&rdquo; - Carrots &#039;N&#039; Cake ,  Home About Press Contact Recipes Appetizers Breakfast Cocktails Desserts Main Dish Salads Snacks Fitness CrossFit Fit Pregnancy Running Workouts Lifestyle Adventures Baby Events Travel Shop Weight Loss All Categories Balanced Eating Beauty & Fashion Boston Celebrities Ulcerative Colitis Home Projects Pug Sponsored Weight Loss Gluten-Free & Egg-Free \u201cCookie Dough\u201d July 3, 2013 Good morning! Happy Hump Day! I visited my new nephew, Matthew, yesterday afternoon. He\u2019s only a day older since the last time I saw him, but he\u2019s already so different. The first day I saw him when he was only 24 hours old, he just slept and didn\u2019t do much. Yesterday, though, he had his eyes open, he was squirming around, and he even sneezed a few times. He\u2019s so cool. Four generations: My sister, Mom, Grammie, and Matthew! Lunch My mom and I brought lunch to my sister\u2019s house yesterday and kept it simple with make-your-own-sandwiches. My sister and her husband have barely slept since Matthew was born, so we wanted to make things as easy as possible for them. We also stocked their fridge with lots of delicious food, so they don\u2019t need to do too much cooking in the coming days while they try to get into a routine with Matthew and begin to adjust to their new life. Snack When I got home from visiting Matthew, I had a major craving for chocolate chip cookie dough, so I got a little creative in the kitchen and whipped up a gluten-free and egg-free batch using almond butter, almond flour, honey, vanilla extract, and white chocolate chips. It turned out so well and totally satisfied my craving\u201d\u201dI just ate it straight from the bowl! Mmm! Ingredients : 2 heaping tbsp creamy almond butter 1/4 cup almond flour 2 tbsp chocolate morsels 1 tsp vanilla extract 1-2 tsp honey 1/8 tsp sea salt Directions : Combine ingredients in a small bowl. Refrigerate for at least 30 minutes. Grab a spoon and enjoy! MY LATEST RECIPES Workout At CrossFit yesterday, the Skill part of our workout was selecting a goal for July, writing it on the Goal Board, and then working on it for 15 minutes. I picked a Muscle Up . I\u2019ve made some decent progress this year with many of my CrossFit skills, but the Muscle Up is just something I haven\u2019t worked on at all. It actually sort of scares me, and, for some reason, I think it\u2019s totally out of my reach, which definitely won\u2019t help me achieve this goal. I figured if I set this goal and aimed high, I\u2019d spend a lot of time working on it and maybe not get a Muscle Up in July, but make enough progress that I will in August or September. I think half the battle is committing to a new goal and actually working at it, so, hopefully, I\u2019ll make some progress in the coming months. Questions of the Day Do you have a niece/nephew? Any tips for being a kick-ass aunt? What are your goals for July? CrossFitters: Any tips for muscle ups? About + Contact About Me Contact Me How I Started Blogging Wedding Recipes Recipes by Category Search My Recipes Running + Fitness Training Plans & Tips Race Recaps & PRs Strength + Ab Exercises Health Tips Blogging Tips How To Start A Blog on WordPress Tips for New Bloggers How to Get More Traffic and Keep Readers Engaged How to Work with Brands as a Blogger Travel Nutrition Coaching Press FAQ General FAQ How to Become a Registered Dietitian How to Start a Nutrition Counseling Private Practice Disclosures & Privacy Policy Microwave Pumpkin Oatmeal Cookie for one October 30, 2013   by Anne 21 Comments Skip To Recipe I have a fun new recipe for you guys this morning! Introducing: a microwave for one! It\u2019s vegan, too. Pumpkin Oatmeal Cookie This healthy, soft, and chewy \u201ccookie\u201d is packed with fiber and healthy fat, making it a great breakfast or snack, and it couldn\u2019t be easier to make \u2013 all you need is the microwave! I was in the mood for something pumpkin-y for breakfast yesterday; I originally considered my Pumpkin Pie Oatmeal  or Pumpkin Pie Smoothie  but I wanted to try something new. Since I had to get down to work, it needed to be fast, and I didn\u2019t want to make anything that would leave a ton of leftovers lying around since we\u2019ll be going out of town this weekend. A single serving oatmeal cookie, made in the microwave? Sounded like a good challenge to me. To add sweetness without needing sugar, I used mashed super ripe banana (applesauce would also work here if you\u2019re not a banana fan) and Almond Breeze  vanilla almondmilk. I also added some nut butter (I used cashew butter, but any kind is fine) and ground flaxseed to help bind it together and add some healthy fats. MY OTHER RECIPES This recipe is perfect for those afternoons when you want something like a cookie\u2026 but that will tide you over for more than 30 seconds. The cookie comes out soft and chewy \u2013 kind of like a muffin top! Serves 1COOKIE adjust servings Microwave Pumpkin Oatmeal Cookie for one Prep Time 5 MINUTES Prep Time Cook Time 5 MINUTES Cook Time Total Time 10 mins Total Time shopping list print Ingredients 1 very ripe banana, mashed (or applesauce - 1/4 C) 3 Tbsp. Almond Breeze vanilla almondmilk 3 Tbsp. rolled oats 2 Tbsp. pumpkin (canned is fine) 1 Tbsp. nut butter (any kind) 3 tsp. raisins or other dried fruit 2 tsp. ground flaxseed 1/2 tsp. pumpkin pie spice 1/4 tsp. cinnamon Instructions Combine and mix all ingredients in a lightly greased/cooking sprayed or nonstick microwave safe bowl. Microwave on high for 4 to 5 minutes. Let cool and enjoy! by Anne @ fANNEtastic food Looks like Matt\u2019s jack-o-lantern wanted a taste, too\u2026 :) I ate the first half of the cookie plain, then decided to mix it up and threw some cottage cheese on top for protein and some blueberries on the side, too. Also delicious! I loved the spiced flavor the pumpkin pie spice and cinnamon gave to it. Very fall-esque. I hope you guys will give this recipe a try and love it as much as I did! Have you ever made a cookie in the microwave before?  I\u2019ve seen a few different microwave cookie recipes floating around on the internet. Then, combine all of the ingredients in the bowl and mix well. Microwave for 60 seconds. Enjoy! {"date_created": 1426928391, "weight": ["76.84", "95.62", "70.98", "27.70", "21.82"], "content": "title: Chocolate Chia Pudding - iFOODreal ,  home about recipes what i ate life travel shop ebooks 25 slow cooker recipes 30 quick dinner recipes pantry & beauty appliances & tools blenders Blendtec protein powder Chocolate Chia Pudding March 20, 2014 74 comments already! Dessert for breakfast anyone?! I mean delicious chocolate dessert with healthy fats, complex carbs, fiber and protein. And only 275 calories. This Chocolate Chia Pudding is creamy, rich and fudgy chocolate heaven. If you tried it with closed eyes, you would think it\u2019s a chocolate mousse. I promise, it\u2019s delicious! I had a hard time deciding on a category for this Chocolate Chia Pudding. Let\u2019s have it for breakfast. Then there is one more thing, besides coffee, to look forward to in the morning. Although I love mornings and you don\u2019t have to kick me out of bed to get up. Especially when I have this waiting for me in the fridge. Oh my. Seeing how much you liked Vanilla Chia Pudding , I was curious to create more. Just wait until Sunday. Even my friend Christi, who is an avid fan of everything butter and cream, bought a bag of chia seeds, made the pudding and loved it! With 3 little kids and a full-time job, she loved the convenience of a 5 minute overnight breakfast. And you can prep chia pudding for up to 5 days in advance. No sugary cereal will beat that. And it\u2019s so easy to make, it\u2019s embarrassing. Add liquids first instead of pouring milk on top of chia seeds and trying to scrape tiny seeds off the bottom of the jar to mix. Plus cocoa/cacao powder takes time to combine evenly with the milk. Recently I switched from cocoa to cacao powder. Raw cacao powder  is unadulterated and contains many more nutrients than traditional cocoa powder. Plus I find it has very rich taste and isn\u2019t more bitter than cocoa powder. Chia seeds themselves are pretty tasteless and expand up to 9 times of their original size. You can add chia to salads, smoothies, baked goods and pretty much anything. I usually buy a 2 lb bag of Nutiva chia seeds at Costco. Just like this one . And a little goes a long way. So, chia is not really expensive if you live in North America. Add chia seeds and cocoa/cacao powder and whisk with a small whisk  (if you have) really well. Until cacao powder is dissolved. Some tiny cacao powder lumps are OK. You will be steering again in the morning. One time my tiny whisk was in the dishwasher, I used fork with no problem to stir the pudding. Refrigerate for at least 6 hours or overnight. When ready to eat, give your chocolate chia pudding another good stir. Sometimes you might have lumps due to gulps of air in-between the chia seeds and that\u2019s OK. There also will be foam on top from whisking the night before. That\u2019s fine too. Just stir really well with a spoon or fork. No whisking is necessary. This chocolate chia pudding is 2 thumbs up. Will pass for a chocolate dessert to anyone with closed eyes. I\u2019m saying that not because it\u2019s my recipe, but because it\u2019s delicious! Chia pudding tastes like something in between tapioca pudding, mousse and Greek yogurt. It melts in your mouth and is creamy and rich. I swear it\u2019s equivalent to eating a chocolate bar but so much healthier. This whole jar for 275 calories. And it\u2019s a perfect breakfast on-the-go. I heard some people do but I do not have any issues with any chia seeds stuck in my mouth afterwards (pardon the details). Well, maximum five. Drink a glass of water after and do your body even more good. I like my chocolate chia pudding to fall off the spoon. Feel free to adjust the consistency to your taste by playing around with the amount of milk. It was my first time trying chia pudding with stevia and I absolutely loved the result. No unpleasant aftertaste as in some baked goods with stevia. Adjust the amount of sweetener to your taste as well. Enjoy! Print Chocolate Chia Pudding Recipe Ingredients 3/4 cup almond (rice, soy, hemp, coconut) milk, unsweetened 2 tsp maple syrup/honey or 1/4 tsp stevia 1 tsp pure vanilla extract 3 - 4 tbsp chia seeds * 1 tbsp cocoa or cacao powder , unsweetened Directions Add all ingredients to a Mason jar  or any container with a tight lid (I prefer glass ) in the order listed above - liquids first. Whisk well or stir vigorously with a fork until cacao powder is well combined with the rest of ingredients. Refrigerate for at least 6 hours or overnight. When ready to eat, stir well again. Some lumps are OK, just stir well. The thickness and sweetness can be adjusted to your taste. Storage Instructions: Refrigerate for up to 5 days. Notes * For a thick consistency pudding use 4 tbsp chia seeds, for soup like consistency (pictured) use only 3 tbsp (my favourite). 3.1 http://ifoodreal.com/chocolate-chia-pudding-recipe/ The recipe and images are property and copyright of iFOODreal.com Nutritional Info Servings Per Recipe: 1 Calories: 275.5 Total Fat: 12 g Cholesterol: 0.0 mg Sodium: 185.2 mg Total Carbs: 28.4 g Dietary Fiber: 17.0 g Protein: 11 g WW Points+: 6 Related Recipes Banana Chia Pudding Vanilla Chia Pudding Healthy Brown Rice Pudding Lemon Blueberry Chia Pudding Coconut Mango Chia Pudding This post may contain affiliate links. {"date_created": 1254891623, "weight": ["92.00", "59.59", "75.13", "90.52", "69.34"], "content": "title: Southern In Law: Recipe: Quick and Easy Stovetop Rice Pudding ,  Tell us what you  would like to see on Southern In Law with our reader request box! Want to follow our adventures? Find us on Facebook , Instagram  or Pinterest! Thursday, August 9, 2012 Recipe: Quick and Easy Stovetop Rice Pudding Did you know that today, August 9th is National Rice Pudding Day? Well.. since I don't live in the US and Australia doesn't have cool food holidays, I'm proudly proclaiming that it is International  Rice Pudding Day! Why? Because everyone should enjoy rice pudding! Today, in celebration of this marvelous day, I wanted to share with you my Quick and Easy Rice Pudding Recipe. It's made on the stovetop and uses leftover rice, saving you tonnes of cooking time! I love to make this rice pudding for breakfast with leftover brown rice and add in dried fruit, nuts, banana, apple or top it with some nut butter! It's healthy, eggless, gluten free, low fat and low sugar (though you can add as much or as little as you like) and can also be made Vegan if you choose a non-dairy milk! What is Rice Pudding? To put it simply, rice pudding is a dish made from rice mixed with milk. Other ingredients can be added and it can be made as a sweet or savoury dish. Personally, I like my rice pudding sweet and mine always needs to have cinnamon! One popular add in for rice pudding is raisins - if you cook them in they plump up and add a delicious flavour! Rice pudding was actually first made in Asia to aid the malnourished, however over thousands of years, thousands of recipes has developed in countries world wide. A traditional English Rice Pudding tends to use milk, sugar and raisins with nutmeg and/or cinnamon. Rice pudding can be baked or made on the stove top with each having a different flavour and consistency. Quick and Easy Stovetop Rice Pudding Recipe Healthy, low fat, eggless, gluten free and delicious - can be vegan too! Serves one! ~1/2 cup cooked rice 3/4 cup milk of your choice 1 tsp vanilla Sugar/sweetener to taste Pinch of salt Optional:  ~1/2 tsp Cinnamon In a small non-stick saucepan, add all of the ingredients. Turn the heat to high and bring mixture to the boil. Once the milk has started to bubble and boil, reduce the heat to medium. Cover the saucepan with a lid and leave to simmer, stirring every now and again. Once the milk really starts to reduce, take the lid off and stir frequently so it doesn't stick to the pan. When it reaches your desired consistency, pour the rice pudding out of the saucepan and into a bowl and leave to cool for a few minutes before eating. Note:  This rice pudding also tastes amazing cold - in the summer I make up a double batch ahead of time and keep it in the fridge. For the rice: In the picture I used cooked brown rice, however, I have also used white rice, red rice and black rice in the past. Before I went gluten free, I also tried it with cooked barley, so I'm sure it would work with other grains as well. For the milk: I generally use low fat cows milk or unsweetened almond milk, but the choice is yours! For the sweetener: For me it has enough sweetness on it's own, but if I'm feeling like it needs more sweetener I will add in a small amount of maple syrup or cane sugar. Feel free to use any sweetener you like - honey, sugar, date sugar, coconut sugar - the list goes on! If you're in a real hurry: Some mornings I just can't be bothered waiting 10-15 minutes for the milk to reduce. On these days, I skip putting the lid on and stir the rice frequently until the milk absorbs. It doesn't make such a creamy consistency but it still tastes delicious. So tell me, are you a rice pudding fan? What do you like to have in yours? Traditionally speaking, I'd have to say cinnamon, raisins and a dash of nutmeg (baked is even better!) - but for breakfast, I love mixing in a mashed banana and topping it with nuts or nut butter or having it with other dried fruit and nuts. My current favourite combination is dates and almond butter! Posted by Kristy Sayer-Jones @ Southern In Law Email This BlogThis! {"date_created": 1130845998, "weight": ["24.85", "95.70", "44.46", "87.09", "33.59"], "content": "title: Mum&#8217;s treat &#8211; moist butterscotch pudding for one | melbournemummy ,  melbournemummy Just another mummy blog Menu Skip to content Home About Little Chop About Me Mum\u2019s treat \u2013 moist butterscotch pudding for\u00a0one Posted on June 9, 2013 by melbournemummy I can\u2019t get enough of these microwave mug cakes at the moment, which isn\u2019t ideal because my plan to walk everyday went out the window last week when I pinched a nerve \u00a0in my back, but on these cold Winter evenings nothing is more comforting than curling up on the couch with a warm cup of cake! Here is my latest offering \u2013 a deliciously moist and caramely butterscotch pudding that\u2019s ready in under five minutes. You\u2019ll need: 1 large mug 1 1/2 tbs milk 2 tsp butter 2 tbs brown sugar 1 tsp honey 3 tbs self-raising flour 1/4 tsp cinnamon 2 1/2 tbs hot water Microwave milk and butter in mug for about 30 seconds or until butter is mostly melted. Add half the brown sugar and microwave again for about 15 seconds then stir until the sugar has dissolved. Mix in the honey and self raising flour until the batter is smooth. Sprinkle the remaining brown sugar and cinnamon over the batter then gently pour the hot water on top. Microwave on high for 60-75 seconds until spongey on top and saucy underneath, then stand for 1-2 minutes. Serve with a dollop of cream or ice-cream. You can thank me later. {"date_created": 1022320984, "weight": ["82.83", "61.46", "22.82", "94.16", "44.70"], "content": "title: THR1VE Blog ,  LOOK FEEL PERFORM TEAM THR1VE VIDEO HOME a blog of inspiration & knowledge curated by the people at THR1VE Raspberry mousse Isabel PM , Recipes No responses July 17, 2013 Do you like dessert? I like dessert and I like it a whole lot. It feels nice to have a special little treat sometimes. I look forward to it, I savour it and I enjoy it during a quiet time when I am relaxed and am winding down for the day. But it wasn\u2019t always like this. Prior to becoming paleo eating dessert used to be followed by mass waves of guilt, shame and self loathing or I felt the need to justify eating it by telling myself that I \u2018deserved\u2019 it as I had been so strict on my diet for 2 weeks beforehand. I was always left wanting more and if left to my own devices found it difficult to stop. To add to these feelings I also suffered bloating and bad skin afterwards. But paleo desserts are different. They are friendly to your insides, don\u2019t leave you suffering from bloating and bad skin, taste amazing yet aren\u2019t packed full of sugar so you feel satisfied afterwards and there is no fear that it is going to increase those dreaded numbers on the scale. So I thought I would share with you my favourite little pink paleo treat that I like to whip up for myself. Raspberry Mousse serves one 2 tablespoons of chia seeds 2 tablespoons of raspberries, frozen or fresh 1 teaspoon of raw honey or stevia granules \u00bd teaspoon of lemon zest, finely grated 2 tablespoons of boiling water 4 tablespoons of the thick coconut cream from a pre-refrigerated can In a teacup or small jar mix together the chia seeds, raspberries, honey or stevia and the lemon zest. Add the boiling water, give it all a good stir and then let it sit for 15 minutes. After 15 minutes the chia seeds should have plumped up and soaked in most of the water. Now stir in the chilled coconut cream until everything is completely combined. You can either eat straight away or pop it back in the fridge for 20 minutes to thicken a little more. TFVG Online Store! What to Cook when you Don't Wanna Cook...a.k.a \"TF... Cookbooks and Ebooks! About Me! \"Link Up with TFVG!\" Friday, May 23, 2014 Silky Peanut Butter Pudding. Peanut. Butter. Pudding. Yes people, it's vegan, gluten free, salt-oil-sugar free, and the WHOLE recipe had less than 150 calories. I'm not kidding! If I was, that would be one cruel joke... Silky Peanut Butter Pudding. Oh  so delicious! Silky Peanut Butter Pudding;  Vegan, Gluten-free. Serves one. Ingredients 1. 5 oz. silken tofu 2. 2 T peanut butter ofchoice (I used \"Just Great Stuff\" brand, which is like PB2) 3. 10 drops liquid stevia Method 1. In your mini food processor, combine silken tofu as peanut butter. If you are using a powdered variety, mix it with 1 T water in a so waste bowl BEFORE adding it to the processor. 2. Blend until smooth, scraping sides as needed. Add stevia once blended and blend again to distribute. 3. Spoon into bowl, top as desired, and EAT! It's also perfectly acceptable to lick the sides of your food processor... Posted by Anna Johnson at 10:12 AM Email This BlogThis! November 18th, 2011 by Michele Miller Are any of you lucky enough to grow or at least have easy access to freshly grown, local bananas and/or\u00a0avocados? Maybe you have an avocado tree in your yard, or perhaps your neighbor does? Oh, and how awesome it would be to have a banana straight from the tree\u2026. However you end up getting the ingredients for this recipe, you are certainly going to be amazed and delighted by how decadent and creamy this pudding is. You don\u2019t taste the avocado so if anyone in your family, or any of your friends, truly detest avocados and won\u2019t eat them, this is such a fun, healthy, and delicious way to sneak them some! Healthful Chocolate Pudding Recipe (serves one) Ingredients: 1 tablespoon raw honey, melted (mine had solidified) 1 banana, frozen 1/2 avocado (it was a big one) 1 tablespoon certified organic cocoa powder 2 tablespoons almond milk, or your choice of milk Directions: Toss all ingredients in to your blender or food processer and blend all the ingredients together \u2018till they\u2019re creamy and smooth. Enjoy immediately! Easy peasy! You can multiply the ingredients by how many you\u2019ll be serving and adjust the recipe accordingly. Kitchen Tip:  Cut or break your bananas in to chunks and . {"date_created": 1453000902, "weight": ["85.39", "52.87", "86.75", "12.87", "58.26"], "content": "title: Banana Soft Serve with Toasted Seeds and Nut Butter Topping  \u2014 Apples Under My Bed ,  Banana Soft Serve with Toasted Seeds and Nut Butter Topping  \u2014 Apples Under My Bed Home Recipes Food & Cooking Motherhood Pregnancy Life About Contact Hi. Welcome to my blog. I write about food, motherhood and all that makes up our days. Apples Under My Bed Nov 5 Nov  5  Banana Soft Serve with Toasted Seeds and Nut Butter Topping Heidi Apples Food & Cooking Good morning, friends. Monday afternoon I posted a picture on my instagram account  of a rather extravagant snack. It involved banana soft serve, nut butter, maple syrup and sea salt. Many appeared to appreciate my concoction and Carly  asked for a recipe, so today I decided to wake a bit earlier, update my previous mention  of banana soft serve and scribe a recipe for Wednesday Breakfast Club . Banana soft serve - what is that ? Well it's really just pureed frozen bananas, maybe with a dash of milk or yoghurt to help move things along. That's it . Banana soft serve (I hesitate to call it ice-cream as though it is creamy in texture it does tend to melt quickly like a soft serve) is outrageously simple and tasty, and after trying it once you'll surely insist on having bags of chopped, frozen bananas in your freezer at all times. For breakfast today, I bedazzled my banana soft serve good and proper with toasted seeds and melted nut butter. Smooth banana cream with rich and sticky nut butter, slightly crunchy flaxmeal and certainly crunchy seeds, plus the sweet pop of syrup and salt. Oh, it was a treat. Banana Soft Serve with Toasted Seeds and Nut Butter Topping Serves one Ingredients 1 frozen Banana 2-3 tablespoons Milk (any kind, eg: cow's or almond) 1 tablespoon Nut Butter (I used a blend of roasted almonds and cashews, similar to this recipe ) 1 tablespoon Sunflower Seeds and Pepitas 1 tablespoon Flaxmeal (ground flax seeds, or LSA mix) 1 teaspoon Pure Maple Syrup Sea Salt Method 1. Toast the seeds in a non-stick pan over low heat for a few minutes until nice and toasty and slightly golden. Set aside. 2. If you nut butter is not drippy, melt it in a small saucepan over low heat, thinning with a tablespoon of milk and whisking as required. Set aside. 3. Puree the frozen banana in a food processor (adding 1-2 tablespoons milk as required) until smooth. 4. Spoon the banana soft serve mixture into a bowl and top with the flaxmeal, nut butter, seeds, maple syrup and a sprinkle of sea salt. Happy soft serve Wednesday! Heidi xo Heidi Apples Food & Cooking Sweets Facebook 0 Twitter Google StumbleUpon Tumblr Pinterest 0 0  Likes Heidi Apples Show 19 comments Heidi Apples Subscribe Email Address Thank you! {"date_created": 1470778694, "weight": ["83.22", "26.87", "91.52", "14.04", "17.29"], "content": "title: Healthy, Homemade Strawberry Coconut Soft Serve ,  Peanut Butter Fingers Living a Life Fueled by Healthy Food and Fitness Navigation Home About Contact Who\u2019s Who All About NASM Disclaimer Wedding Recipe Index Workouts Pregnancy Baby Shop + Favs Blogging Books Travel Orlando & Florida Blog Travel Strawberry Coconut Soft Serve May 15, 2013  by Julie 73 Comments This sweet frozen treat is perfect when you need a quick and healthy dessert but don\u2019t want to go out to a fancy frozen yogurt shop. Pick your favorite frozen fruits, blend and enjoy! I love getting soft serve and frozen yogurt from fancy shops, but sometimes the cravings come on fast and furious at home, especially after we take the dog for a walk or spend some time outside. I created this recipe one night when I opened the freezer to search for something sweet and cold and found myself facing a giant bag of frozen strawberries. Along with the frozen strawberries, I grabbed some frozen raspberries and took out my blender, determined to make a cold and creamy dessert. I also had a can of coconut milk in the pantry and decided to give it a try, and the end result was a fantastic bowl of strawberry coconut soft serve! Save Print Strawberry Coconut Soft Serve Prep time: 5 mins Total time: 5 mins Serves: 1 This sweet frozen treat is perfect when you need a quick and healthy dessert but don't want to go out to a fancy frozen yogurt shop. Pick your favorite frozen fruits, blend and enjoy! Ingredients 1 cup frozen strawberries \u00bc cup raspberries \u00bc cup light coconut milk (plus more, if needed, to get everything moving) Tiny splash coconut extract Shredded coconut for garnish Instructions Combine strawberries, raspberries and coconut milk in a high-powered blender or food processor. Blend until smooth and creamy (several minutes). Add coconut extract to taste. (Note: Start with a very small amount and increase gradually. Coconut extract is very strong!) Scoop soft serve into a bowl and garnish with shredded coconut. 3.5.3226 If you are a banana-lover, feel free to add half of a frozen banana (and likely a little more coconut milk) to the mix to make the soft serve even creamier! And if you\u2019d rather not use coconut milk, you can easily use almond, soy or regular milk in its place, but, if you choose to do this, I would definitely add half of a frozen banana to keep the soft serve nice and creamy. Enjoy! Be sure to follow PBFingers on Instagram and Facebook! I'd love to connect with you! I am always so grateful when you let me know you tried one of my recipes or workouts and tag me in your photos or updates. Thank you so much!!! This weekend we had peanut butter chocolate chip, but the possibilities are endless. For Valentine\u2019s Day I made a Cherry Garcia flavor with frozen bananas, frozen cherries, chocolate chips, and vanilla extract. We always have bananas in the freezer, just in case, but they only need to freeze for a few hours if you don\u2019t already have a stash. Print Peanut Butter Chocolate Chip Ice Cream Author: Christine Recipe type: dessert, raw, vegan Serves: 1 I always keep bananas in the freezer for this exact reason. This recipe serves one. Throw in as many bananas as you'd like servings. Ingredients 1 Frozen banana 1-2 Tbsp peanut butter 1-2 Tbsp chocolate chips (I like Enjoy Life ones, or you make raw ones) 1-2 Tbsp non-dairy milk (I use almond milk, but coconut makes it very creamy also) Vanilla (optional) Cinnamon (optional) Instructions Blend the banana and the milk. {"date_created": 1166451974, "weight": ["60.02", "96.84", "13.35", "19.03", "48.03"], "content": "title: Single serving deep dish apple pie | for Thom, with love | Oh, Ladycakes ,  About About OLC FAQ Press Recipes Recipe index The Evolution of a Recipe Kitchen essentials Travel Denver, CO Iceland Denmark + Sweden Ireland Bolivia + Peru Morocco Reads Contact Subscribe Single serving deep dish apple pie | for Thom, with love Introducing for Thom, with love \u00a0\u2013 a new series documenting the small batch recipes I create for , chock full of love. Over the course of the past half decade, I\u2019ve witnessed Thom eat his fair share of baked goods \u2013 and in the process I discovered that sometimes\u00a0all he needs is a single serving of chocolate chip cookies because the man has no self control when cookies are involved.\u00a0And if you leave an entire batch at his disposal, he\u2019ll eat them all and ask you to make more.\u00a0Then he\u2019ll eat those, too, and complain about his stomach aching and you\u2019ll decide it\u2019s time to start developing small batch recipes.\u00a0So if your favorite person is like Thom, surely they\u2019ll appreciate these recipes.\u00a0And so will you because they can be thrown together without having to dirty heavy mixing machines or three baking sheets or every single measuring device you own. my favorite man The recipes, they\u2019re good. Straight forward and equally as delicious as a full batch, but without all of the elbow grease required to scoop 36 cookies or roll out a 10\u2033 pie crust. The selling point, for me, is that small batch recipes don\u2019t produce any waste. Not\u00a0that anything really goes to waste around here because I\u2019m the lady who shows up at my neighbor\u2019s door at 10 o\u2019clock at night, begging her to take a container of brownies away because Bad things will happen if you don\u2019t. \u00a0The other selling point is the expression on Thom\u2019s face when he realizes I\u2019ve made something special just for him. Friends, I\u2019ve been saying it for years: the best way to a man\u2019s heart is, without a doubt, through his stomach. Notes:\u00a0If you prefer a sweeter pie crust, feel free to increase the sugar to one full teaspoon. But I promise you won\u2019t require it if you fill the pie with the full 6 teaspoons (2 tablespoons) of sugar. This recipe requires the use of one deep dish 4\u2033 tartlet pan (although I suppose a ramekin would work, as well). I got my tartlet pans in a set at , but if you like getting ripped off, you can get them individually at Williams-Sonoma (my least favorite kitchen store in the history of kitchen stores) (look at the price difference per tart pan \u2013 $5.66). Greedy asswads. Sur la Table SINGLE SERVING DEEP DISH APPLE PIE Crust 1/2 cup unbleached flour 1/2 tsp cane sugar Pinch of fine sea salt 3 tbsp vegan butter , cold 2-3 tbsp water , ice cold Filling 4-6 tsp cane sugar 1 tsp potato starch 1/4 tsp ground cinnamon One medium apple , peeled and chopped 1/2 tsp lemon juice , optional Preheat oven to 350\u02daF. Lightly oil a 4\u2033 deep dish tart pan; set aside. In a small mixing bowl, whisk together the flour, sugar, and salt. Cut in the butter, using a pastry cutter or two knives, until the mixture resembles coarse meal with a few larger chunks. Add two tablespoons of the water and mix with fingers until a smooth dough forms. If the dough feels a little dry, add a bit more water. Knead the dough for 1-2 minutes then wrap with plastic and let rest in the refrigerator for 30 minutes. To make the filling, stir together the sugar (I used 5 teaspoons), starch, and cinnamon. Add the apples and lemon juice; toss to coat and set aside. Line a flat surface with parchment paper and sprinkle with flour. Roll the dough into a circle about 1/4\u2033 thick. Fit to prepared tart pan, making sure it\u2019s pressed into the bottom into the scalloped edges. Roll a rolling pin over the top of the pan to remove the excess dough. Fill with apples. Roll the remaining dough scraps, cut with a mini heart shaped cookie cutter (dip in flour if sticking to dough), and arrange on top of pie. Brush with a bit of soy milk and sprinkle with sugar, if desired. Bake at 350\u02daF for 35-40 minutes (if you notice the hearts starting to brown, put a piece of tin foil over top of them after about 25 minutes). Let cool for 10 minutes then serve. Can be refrigerated in an air tight container for up to two days. If you\u2019d prefer to assemble the pie and save it for later, remove the pie from the freezer when ready to bake and let it thaw for about 20 minutes. Follow baking instructions above. Unbaked pie will keep frozen for up to 6 weeks in an air tight, freezer proof container. Yield: 1 4\u2033 pie 45 Comments Share: 45 Comments Reply Taylor 7 May 2013 at 1:36 PM So cute! {"date_created": 1389938650, "weight": ["90.84", "51.26", "71.13", "57.09", "38.46"], "content": "title: One Minute Blueberry Cobbler Recipe - Snappy Gourmet ,  Skip to primary navigation Skip to content Skip to primary sidebar Skip to footer Search this website Snappy Gourmet Fun food that's a snap to make!
