Desserts Drinks Main Dishes Salads Side Dishes Soups & Stews Slow Cooker Travel / Shopping Fun Finds Travel Variety of shopping guides from Snappy Gourmet including favorite kitchen products, ideas for kids who like to cook, etc. Shopping Resources Free E-Book Food Holidays & Recipes January Food Holidays February Food Holidays March Food Holidays April Food Holidays May Food Holidays June Food Holidays July Food Holidays August Food Holidays September Food Holidays October Food Holidays November Food Holidays December Food Holidays Giveaways Shop Contact Books Home  \u00bb One Minute Blueberry Cobbler (single serving) One Minute Blueberry Cobbler (single serving) August 1, 2012 41 Comments Pin it for later Pin Share Tweet Yum +1 Stumble One Minute Blueberry Cobbler, an easy blueberry cobbler recipe made in the microwave for one person. (For your shopping convenience, this post contains affiliate links.) Yep, you can make this easy single serving Blueberry Cobbler  recipe in ONE MINUTE!!\u00a0 And it was quite tasty if I do say so myself!\u00a0 Thumbs up from the family and they\u2019ve actually been requesting these simple blueberry cobblers on a regular basis now. You do need a few minutes to prepare these cobblers, but each blueberry cobbler only takes one minute to cook in the microwave.\u00a0 These single serving berry cobblers are perfect to make if you only want to make one or two servings instead of making\u00a0a huge pan in the oven. These single serving cobblers are also\u00a0great if you have a late night craving and need something quick! I cut way back on the sugar and used simple ingredients but I bet you won\u2019t miss it all! If blueberry isn\u2019t your thing, I also have a recipes for Individual Strawberry Cobblers \u00a0and Amaretto Caramel Apple Mug Cobblers . Instead of blueberries you could also try different fruit in this recipe. This easy blueberry cobbler recipe comes\u00a0together quick! These are meant to be an easy QUICK fix if you\u2019re craving something sweet. No, it\u2019s NOT\u00a0just as good as a big sugary gooey blueberry cobbler out of the oven that took all day to make (so don\u2019t send me nasty emails\u2026), but it\u2019s still tasty especially with a little ice cream or whipped cream on top. First, mix together all the dry ingredients, flour, sugar, and baking powder.\u00a0 Add a pinch of salt if you\u2019d like. You could add a little cinnamon or spices. Then mix in your milk and melted butter to the batter. Place your blueberries in the bottom of your ramekin.\u00a0 You\u2019ll need a large ramekin  (8 oz.).\u00a0You could also substitute a large microwave safe mug  or small bowl. This would work well like a mug cake recipe. I did not add any sugar to my blueberries, but if you like your blueberry cobblers really sweet add a little sugar or even maple syrup. You could also add a little cornstarch or flour if you want the fruit juices to thicken up.\u00a0 I really didn\u2019t think it needed it. Press down on your blueberries a little with the back of a spoon or fork to make room for the topping. For a little extra flavor you could add a little vanilla extract, almond extract, or even maple extract. Spoon your cobbler topping on top of the blueberries in a nice even layer. Place the ramekin on top of a small microwave safe plate JUST in case the blueberries boil over a little.\u00a0 Sometimes mine do, sometimes they don\u2019t. Microwave the blueberry cobbler on high for 30 seconds, check on it, then microwave another 30 seconds. You may have to adjust the time slightly for your particular microwave.\u00a0 Microwaving for 2 intervals of 30 seconds seemed to help prevent the blueberries from boiling over too much by giving them just enough time to cool down slightly. Top with your favorite ice cream , whipped topping, or whipped cream if you\u2019d like. And there you go, an easy single serving microwave blueberry cobbler ready in no time. Wasn\u2019t that quick and easy for a fresh blueberry cobbler?\u00a0 Only 6 ingredients, a few minutes to prep, and 1 minute in the microwave for a quick and easy single serving blueberry cobbler!!! This easy blueberry cobbler recipe is the perfect quick sugar fix! Great in the summer when fresh blueberries are abundant. Here\u2019s a quick video to show how fast these cobblers are to put together\u2026 You could also try defrosted frozen berries if you don\u2019t want to wait until summer! I hope you enjoy these cute mini blueberry cobblers! Thanks for visiting! 3.84  from 6  votes Print One Minute Blueberry Cobbler Quick and easy blueberry cobbler recipe that can be made in just 1 minute! Course Dessert Cuisine American Prep Time 5 minutes Cook Time 1 minute Total Time 6 minutes Yield 1 Author Snappy Gourmet - Lisa Huff Ingredients 1/4 cup all-purpose flour 2 teaspoons sugar 1/4 teaspoon baking powder pinch of salt 2 tablespoons milk 2 teaspoons unsalted butter melted 1/2 cup fresh blueberries Toppings (optional): ice cream, whipped topping, or whipped cream Instructions In a small bowl, mix together flour, sugar, baking powder, and salt until well combined. Mix in milk and melted butter until just combined. Place blueberries in bottom of a large (8 oz.) microwave safe ramekin or microwave safe mug. Press blueberries down slightly with the back of a fork to break up. Spoon batter on top of blueberries. Place cobbler on top of small microwave safe plate in case blueberries boil over. Microwave on high for 30 seconds, check on cobbler, then microwave another 30 seconds. Adjust baking time as needed for your microwave. Top with your favorite ice cream, whipped topping, or whipped cream if desired. Recipe Notes SNAPPY TIPS: I have only made these cobblers 1 at a time in the microwave. You can make multiple cobblers at a time but will need to adjust cooking time. Do not overfill your ramekin/mug or it will boil over a lot. For a little more flavor add a little vanilla extract, almond extract, or other flavoring to the topping or fruit. SNAPPY SUBSTITUTIONS: Instead of blueberries, try other fruit but some fruit may need to be precooked. You can also add a little sugar or maple syrup to the blueberries or add a little flour or cornstarch if you want the juices to thicken up. You can also add cinnamon or other spices to your cobbler topping or blueberries. (a food blog) A collection of recipes and food-related items. Skip to content About Search for: Pecan Pie in a\u00a0Mug April 21, 2012 Uncategorized microwave , mug , pecanpie foozma73 more from Roni via email. Pecan          Pie in a Mug 1-1/2 tablespoons butter or margarine 3 tablespoons finely chopped pecans 3 tablespoons brown sugar,          packed 1 tablespoon flour 2 teaspoons egg white powder 1/2          tablespoon instant nonfat dry milk 1/8 teaspoon vanilla powder          (optional) 1/16 teaspoon baking powder Dash of salt 3          tablespoons of water Microwave butter or margarine in mug until          melted, about 20 seconds on high power. Add remaining ingredients          and stir with a fork until blended. Microwave on 60 percent power for          2 minutes. Let stand in the microwave 1 to 2 minutes. Remove          from oven and let stand until cool enough to eat. Note: 1 egg          equals 2 tablespoons egg powder and 2 tablespoons warm water. Adjust          the recipes accordingly. Author: Jen @ Jen's Favorite Cookies Recipe type: Dessert Serves: 1 Ingredients 1 cup (3.75 oz) diced peaches 1 tablespoon flour 2 tablespoon rolled oats 2 tablespoons brown sugar dash salt 2 teaspoons butter Instructions Drain peaches and place in a ramekin. Add flour and toss to coat. Sprinkle oats and brown sugar over the top. Add salt. Cut pieces of butter on top. Bake at 350F for 15-20 minutes, until crust is brown. Single Serving Apple Crisp 1 small apple 2 tbsp. brown sugar 2 tbsp. oats 1 1/2 tbsp. flour 1/4 tsp. cinnamon 1 tbsp. butter Thinly slice the apple and place in a mixing bowl. Add 1 tbsp. brown sugar, 1/2 tbsp. flour, and 1/8 tsp. cinnamon. Coat the apples with the dry ingredients and place in a small baking dish. Mix together the rest of the dry ingredients and the butter; put on top of the apples. Microwave for 60-90 seconds. Check out some other single serving recipes! {"date_created": 1280107372, "weight": ["73.13", "24.34", "65.70", "73.03", "37.76"], "content": "title: Recipe: Pumpkin Pie in a Mug | Kitchn ,  Facebook Pinterest Instagram Email Search Everyday Cooking Meal Planning Grocery Shopping Budget Smart Tips Kitchn Meal Plans Kitchn Menus How To Cooking Lessons Baking Lessons Knife Lessons Meat Lessons Pro Technique Surprising Ideas Cooking School Baking School Living Family Travel Kitchn Life At Home With Make More Good Bake a Day Off Organizing & Cleaning Cleaning Cleaning Tools Organizing Rental Kitchens Pantry Set Up a Kitchen Gather Kitchn Gatherings Cocktails Dinner for a Crowd Great Gifts Weddings Etiquette Holidays Gift Guides Wellness Shopping Recipes Breakfast Lunch Dinner Snacks Dessert Cocktails Baking Videos Recipe: Pumpkin Pie in a Mug Recipes from The Kitchn Recipe: Pumpkin Pie in a Mug Print Recipe Faith Durand Nov 3, 2017 Autumn Butter Cake Dessert Easy Halloween Microwaves Pie Quick Recipe Snack Sweets Thanksgiving Video Share Pin It Email Share Pin It Email Share Pin It Email Share Pin It Email (Image credit: Faith Durand ) If you love pumpkin pie and just can't wait until Thanksgiving dinner to taste your first slice, then I have a dessert for you. This is a little cup of pumpkin pie, mug cake-style, with a gingersnap crust and snappy spices, and it feeds just one person: you. Make it in a mug, in the microwave, and you can be eating pumpkin pie 10 minutes from right now. Yes, this is a mug pie (not to be confused with a mudpie ) but it falls somewhere between a pie and a cake in texture. It's a little treat for those of you who adore pumpkin and spiced fall desserts, and it's a quick and easy way to give yourself a sweet ending to a long day without baking an entire pie. Like other mug cakes baked in the microwave, its texture is soft and a little spongy. There's a satisfying base of gingersnap crumbs in butter, too; they don't crisp up like they would in the oven but I love the way they complement the taste of the pumpkin. The pumpkin comes through boldly; if you have homemade squash puree lying about this is a great use for it. I sweeten it up with brown sugar and spice it with pumpkin pie spice, but feel free to substitute honey, maple syrup, or other sweeteners, and to use your own mixes of spices instead of a packaged pumpkin pie spice. (Image credit: Faith Durand ) More Mug Cakes Oatmeal Nutella Mug Cake 13 Easy Microwave Mug Cakes That Are All Grown Up Mug-Cake Pumpkin Pie: Watch the Video Pumpkin Pie Mug Cake Makes 1 1 teaspoon unsalted butter 14 grams gingersnaps (2 small cookies), crushed into 2 tablespoons of crumbs 1/3 cup pumpkin puree 1 large egg 1 tablespoon milk or cream 2 tablespoons brown sugar 1 teaspoon pumpkin pie spice Place the butter in a microwave-safe mug that holds at least 10 ounces, and microwave on LOW until melted. Stir in the crushed gingersnaps and press the mixture firmly into the bottom of the mug. In a separate small bowl, whisk together the pumpkin puree, egg, milk or cream, brown sugar, and pumpkin pie spice. Pour into mug with the gingersnap \"crust.\" Place the mug on a microwave-safe plate. Microwave on full power for 2 to 5 minutes, or until a knife inserted in the center of the mug pie comes out clean. The top may look slightly damp but it will set as it cools. (Cooking time will vary greatly depending on your microwave and the width and depth of the mug. Start with 2 minutes and continue cooking in 30-second increments until it is done.) Use a hot pad or oven mitt to carefully remove the mug from the microwave. Let it stand for a couple minutes to cool, then top, if desired, with whipped cream and crushed nuts before eating. Recipe Notes Doubling the recipe:  You can double this recipe, but only cook one mug pie in the microwave at a time. {"date_created": 1261223655, "weight": ["87.99", "95.82", "32.40", "92.22", "76.72"], "content": "title: Single-Serving Pumpkin Cinnamon Rolls | Healthy Aperture ,  Single-Serving Pumpkin Cinnamon Rolls | Healthy Aperture Login badges | contact Menu Home About Videos Shop Blog FAQ Submit Get Our FREE Cookbook! From cookies to bars, breads to muffins you're sure to find something special to bake in this FREE cookbook -- Healthy Everyday Baking. DOWNLOAD your copy today! Blog \u00bb Single-Serving Pumpkin Cinnamon Rolls Single-Serving Pumpkin Cinnamon Rolls Posted by immaeatthat September 10, 2014 Featured in: The Garden Jump to recipe Looking for a small batch recipe to do some fall baking? Try this single serving cinnamon roll made with pumpkin. by Kylie Mitchell It\u2019s pumpkin time again (\"insert pumpkin emoji here\u201d)!! I really want to incorporate more savory pumpkin things into my life this fall.\u00a0 It\u2019s not gonna be all pumpkin muffins , pumpkin scones  and pumpkin pancakes  for me.\u00a0 No, this year I\u2019m going to branch out.\u00a0 I\u2019ve been dreaming of pumpkin gnocchi with arugula for like 3 weeks now.\u00a0 But before I go all savory pumpkin, I had to go sweet pumpkin. I make pumpkin breakfast bakes  all year round.\u00a0 Pumpkin puree does something to the texture of breakfast bakes that nothing else can.\u00a0 Other than breakfast bakes, I save all baked pumpkin goods for September thru December.\u00a0 That way they seem like something special around the holidays. I\u2019m not sure when, but at some point in my life I stopped carving pumpkins and started eating them.\u00a0 Is this a life change everyone goes through?\u00a0 I never remember eating the vegetable when I was a kid.\u00a0 Even during the holidays I didn\u2019t touch pumpkin pie because there was always something chocolaty that I preferred.\u00a0 But at some defining moment I realized the wonder pumpkin can add to one's life. I took one bite of these pumpkin cinnamon rolls to taste test them and then I ummm\u2026ate them all.\u00a0 I should\u2019ve known this would happen.\u00a0 I have rather limited self-control with cinnamon rolls.\u00a0 They are easily my favorite baked good ever.\u00a0 Layers of dough + layers of cinnamon-sugar.\u00a0 Hello, beautiful.\u00a0 It\u2019s like the most perfect thing ever.\u00a0 And now we\u2019ve added pumpkin to those layers, so all you pumpkin spice latte lovers out there should definitely get behind this. I never order cinnamon rolls when I\u2019m at a restaurant because you can\u2019t control the gooeyness.\u00a0 I\u2019m a big advocate for gooey things. True story: I ordered a cinnamon roll at Disneyland when I was little and it was like the worst experience of my life.\u00a0 It should have been the best cinnamon roll ever since, ya know, DISNEY!\u00a0 But then I tasted it and it was flaky and dry like a crossiant and not ooey and gooey like my favorite thing.\u00a0 Ugh such a let down.\u00a0 I think that was probably the last cinnamon roll I ordered out.\u00a0 I learned my lesson.\u00a0 If Disney can't get it right...no one can. Now I really do love making homemade cinnamon rolls.\u00a0 I do I do I do.\u00a0 I love sprinkling on the filling, rolling up the dough into that classic cinnamon roll shape and slicing up the dough into little, fluffy rolls.\u00a0 I do not however like waiting for cinnamon rolls to rise.\u00a0 That is why I went the yeast-free route for this single-serving pumpkin version. We should address the fact that these pumpkin cinnamon rolls are only loosely sticking to the Global Garden theme.\u00a0 Pumpkin is the only ingredient in this recipe that grows in a garden.\u00a0 But it\u2019s almost fall, which is reason for pumpkin-infused celebration, ya know? If you think making a single-serving cinnamon roll seems like the most selfish thing ever, you could always double the recipe.\u00a0 And I will come eat it with you.\u00a0 And we will be best friends. Single-serving Pumpkin Cinnamon Rolls Yield Serves 1 (makes 2 baby cinnamon rolls) Ingredients Dough: 1/4 cup oat flour, packed 1/4 cup whole wheat flour 1/4 teaspoon baking powder 1/8 teaspoon baking soda 3-1/2 tablespoons pumpkin puree 1 tablespoon butter, softened 1/4 teaspoon vanilla Filling: 2 teaspoons brown sugar 1/2 teaspoon cinnamon 1 scant teaspoon butter, softened Icing: Greek yogurt honey Directions Preheat oven to 350F.\u00a0 In a bowl, combine oat flour, whole wheat flour, baking powder, baking soda and salt.\u00a0 Add in pumpkin puree, butter and vanilla.\u00a0\u00a0 Use a spoon (or your hands) to combine until a dough forms. In a separate bowl, combine brown sugar and cinnamon. Lightly flour a flat surface.\u00a0 Roll dough into a ball.\u00a0 Now roll dough back and forth between your hands to make a long cylinder of dough.\u00a0 Place the dough onto the floured surface and press flat.\u00a0 Spread butter over the top and sprinkle on the brown sugar-cinnamon.\u00a0 Roll dough up into a cinnamon roll shape and cut roll in half to make two cinnamon rolls.\u00a0 Place the cinnamon rolls into a greased ramekin.\u00a0 Bake for 12 minutes for gooey cinnamon rolls or 16 minutes for fully cooked cinnamon rolls.\u00a0 Stir together greek yogurt and honey.\u00a0 Drizzle over the top. {"date_created": 1074462404, "weight": ["69.07", "57.38", "52.47", "14.70", "22.86"], "content": "title: Brownie A La Anytime - Single Serving Brownies Made In The Microwave - Love From The Oven ,  Home Recipes Bread Breakfast Brownies and Bars Cakes & Cupcakes Candy Cookies Desserts Drinks Frozen Pets Pie Pops Savory Sprinkles Holiday Recipes Valentine\u2019s Day St. Patrick\u2019s Day Easter 4th Of July Halloween Thanksgiving Christmas New Year\u2019s Eve Birthdays Printables Blog \u2191 Love From The Oven Away From The Oven Love From The Oven Easy and delicious recipes. About Contact Brands/PR Faq Home Recipes Bread Breakfast Brownies and Bars Cakes & Cupcakes Candy Cookies Desserts Drinks Frozen Pets Pie Pops Savory Sprinkles Holiday Recipes Valentine\u2019s Day St. Patrick\u2019s Day Easter 4th Of July Halloween Thanksgiving Christmas New Year\u2019s Eve Birthdays Printables Blog Don't Miss Out, Subscribe  Now! #LoveFromTheOven Brownie A La Anytime \u2013 Single Serving Brownies Made In The Microwave While I love almost all desserts, to me the BEST desserts fall into the \u201ca la mode\u201d category.\u00a0 They are warm and topped with ice cream, and that combo takes almost any dessert to a whole other level.\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0 I LOVE A La Mode. For a while I\u2019ve been trying to come up with a quick and easy way to make an individual serving of brownie a la mode at home, and the results aren\u2019t always the best.\u00a0\u00a0 Some have turned out like this\u2026 We\u2019ll call those Brownie A La Garbage Disposal.\u00a0 Bleh.\u00a0\u00a0 I tried using mixes, thinking that would be a nice way to keep it easy, but I was never happy with the results.\u00a0 Today I decided to work on one based on my favorite brownie recipe  and see what I could create, and I think we have a winner. Yeah, this recipe is a keeper.\u00a0\u00a0 Hot, gooey, dark chocolatey brownies in a few short minutes using the microwave and simple ingredients???\u00a0\u00a0 We\u2019ll call them Brownies A La Anytime. Here is what you need\u2026 At the very last moment I decided that I wanted to add baking powder, so this guy didn\u2019t make it into the photo, but he made it into the brownies.\u00a0\u00a0 The ingredients are as follows.\u00a0 This will make one generous serving.\u00a0\u00a0 It could be shared, if you are feeling generous, but I won\u2019t judge you if you keep it all to yourself. Brownies A La Anytime 4 Tablespoons Flour 3 Tablespoons Sugar Pinch Of Salt 1/8 teaspoon Baking Powder 2 Tablespoons Cocoa Powder (I prefer Hershey\u2019s Dark Cocoa Powder) 1 Tablespoon Melted Butter 1-2 Tablespoons Oil (such as vegetable, canola or coconut) 1 Tablespoon Water 1/4 Teaspoon Vanilla You can top with a few chocolate chips or nuts if you like. Melt your butter in a microwave safe bowl or cup (took me about 12 seconds).\u00a0\u00a0 Add the oil to your melted butter and mix well. If you want a moister brownie, go for the full two tablespoons.\u00a0 I prefer a really solid, dense brownie (which I top with ice cream adding a lot of moisture) so I use one tablespoon of oil.  \u00a0 Add in your vanilla and water, stir well to combine.\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0 In a separate bowl or cup, combine all dry ingredients. As I said, I used only one tablespoon of oil, so my mix is a bit on the drier/firm side.\u00a0\u00a0 I pressed it into my ramekin.\u00a0\u00a0 You could also use a mug, microwaving things in a mug seems to be the popular thing, but being a non-coffee drinker (hello, Diet Coke!), I have more ramekins than I do mugs. I added a few chocolate chips to the top. I started with 45 seconds in the microwave and ended up cooking mine for about one minute and ten seconds.\u00a0 That\u2019s 70 seconds people \u2013 until hot, gooey, delicious, dark, sweet chocolate goodness.\u00a0\u00a0 SEVENTY SECONDS!\u00a0\u00a0 That\u2019s like magic! Instant.\u00a0 Gratification.\u00a0\u00a0 Which is both a very good, and possibly very bad, thing.\u00a0\u00a0 These may be too easy to whip up! In my opinion, anything \u201ca la mode\u201d needs ice cream.\u00a0 End of story. These are best enjoyed within a few minutes of heating them up.\u00a0\u00a0 I have a few yummy variations coming up, but I have to pace myself, eating four of these in a day is probably not recommended.\u00a0 Though it would be damn delicious.\u00a0\u00a0 ENJOY! {"date_created": 984118345, "weight": ["84.17", "68.87", "85.96", "81.82", "78.04"], "content": "title: Peanut Butter Balls for One | Wit &amp; Whistle ,  Skip to content Shop New Cards Holiday Single Cards Seasonal Valentine\u2019s Day Mother\u2019s Day Father\u2019s Day Easter Halloween Thanksgiving Holiday Birthday Love + Friendship Babies + Grads + Congrats Thank You Wedding + Engagement Get Well + Sympathy Just Because Boxed Cards Notecard Sets Holiday Sets Pins Notepads Pencils Prints Sale Wholesale Stores About Blog Contact 0 items Peanut Butter Balls for One I get excited for Christmas when September arrives, so I\u2019ve been craving a Christmassy dessert lately. Peanut Butter Balls are my holiday go to, but my recipe  makes a zillion and calls for an entire pound of butter (no wonder I start every new year with muffin top). After a little experimenting I\u2019ve found the perfect peanut butter/butter/powdered sugar ratio to make only THREE peanut butter balls! It takes 5 minutes, and they\u2019re perfect for when you\u2019re craving a super rich dessert, but don\u2019t want a bunch of leftovers hanging around to tempt you later. A plastic fork with the center two prongs snapped off is the perfect chocolate dipping tool. It allows the excess chocolate drip right off. The chocolate isn\u2019t nearly as shiny and smooth as it is when I melt it in my double boiler  with a little paraffin wax, but it really doesn\u2019t matter what they look like\u2026 because I\u2019m going to promptly eat every last one of them. Just for the record, dear Ohioans, these are not buckeyes. To be a buckeye a peanut butter ball must have part of the peanut butter center left un-chocolate coated, and I think that is a wasted opportunity! ;) Here\u2019s the recipe! 4 teaspoons peanut butter 1 tablespoon softened butter 1/4 cup (slightly heaping) powdered sugar 1/4 cup semisweet chocolate chips Stir together the peanut butter and butter until they are well combined and smooth. Stir in the powdered sugar. Roll the dough into three balls.\u00a0Melt the chocolate chips in the microwave, and\u00a0coat the peanut butter balls in chocolate. Let the chocolate set and harden a bit\u00a0(stick them in the fridge if you\u2019re impatient), and enjoy! 35 Comments September 4, 2012 Post navigation \u2190  Hand Lettering Practice #3 Spider Appreciation Day \u2192 35 comments Lindsey September 4, 2012 at 6:54 pm Oh yum! I switched the recipe up a tiny bit by heating the butter and peanut butter before adding the powdered sugar. I also added a pinch of sea salt ( I found my peanut butter a tad sweet) and a dash of vanilla bean paste. I chilled this in the fridge while I scooped three 3/4\u2033 scoops of ganache and quickly rolled it in my hands into balls. I popped those in the freezer to firm up a tad. Once they were cool I wrapped them in the peanut batter and rolled them to smooth them. I rolled these in a dusting of cocoa powder and/or powdered sugar. {"date_created": 1099679110, "weight": ["28.83", "64.14", "25.10", "96.08", "78.66"], "content": "title: The 5-Minute, Single-Serving, Raw Vegan Blondie | Chef Amber Shea ,  Chef Amber Shea Practical. Home Recipes Breakfast Desserts Drinks Gluten-Free Low-Calorie Low-Fat Main Dishes Raw Snacks & Sides Soups & Salads About Me Frequently Asked Questions Culinary School My Cookbooks Practically Raw Autographed Copies Practically Raw Desserts Autographed Copies The REAL FOOD Cleanse Reviews Books Food (general) Gluten-Free Juice Cleanses Raw Food Snack Bars Supplements Sweet Treats Other Travels Boston area, MA Buffalo, NY Chicago, IL Dallas, TX Denver, CO Des Moines, IA Europe Austria England France Germany Greece Italy Netherlands Spain Switzerland Turkey Kansas City, MO Las Vegas, NV Lawrence, KS Los Angeles, CA Minneapolis, MN Oklahoma City, OK Portland, OR San Francisco Bay Area Springfield, MO Toronto, Ontario Western Mexico Wichita, KS Wedding Cake Ceremony D\u00e9cor Dress Food & Drink Guest Favors Invitations Music Rings Venue Video Contact Browse: Home / 2011 / January / 22 / The 5-Minute, Single-Serving, Raw Vegan Blondie The 5-Minute, Single-Serving, Raw Vegan Blondie By on Chef Amber Shea January 22, 2011 | Posted in Desserts , Gluten-Free , Raw , Recipes 152 Comments HAPPY NATIONAL BLONDIE DAY! That\u2019s right\u2014today, January 22nd, is apparently National Blondie Day. Since I consider myself a bit of a blondie queen , I couldn\u2019t possibly let it pass by unnoticed, now could I? I found out about this \u201choliday\u201d on Thursday night, as I was riding the emotional high that your kind comments  lent me. One particular comment  stuck out to me. Brenda said: Now, go dream up some wonderful super easy recipe for me to try out. So I did.  And wouldn\u2019t you know, it was a smashing success on the very first try! This recipe: uses common ingredients works with a variety of substitutions takes less than 5 minutes to prepare from start to finish requires only one piece of equipment (food processor) conveniently makes just one serving doesn\u2019t require any advance prep does NOT require baking OR dehydration provides instant gratification It also happens to be: raw vegan gluten-free grain-free dairy-free oil-free and frickin\u2019 DELICIOUS! So here it is, folks. This is the treat I spontaneously concocted in my kitchen on Thursday night, thanks in large part to YOU. Consider it my little way of saying \u201cthank you,\u201d again . Print The 5-Minute, Single-Serving, Raw Vegan Blondie Yield: 1 generous serving Ingredients 1/4 cup dry macadamia nuts or cashews 1/4 cup dry walnuts or pecans 2 tablespoons coconut palm sugar 2 to 3 pitted dates 1/8 teaspoon vanilla extract Big pinch of sea salt Cacao nibs, for garnish (optional) Instructions Combine the nuts and sugar in a mini food processor.  (A mini one works best, but I think a regular-sized one would be fine. Or you could just quadruple the recipe and make a family-size blondie!) Pulse the nuts and sugar together until the mixture is ground into a coarse powder. Add the dates, one at a time, pulsing several times between additions, until each date is well-incorporated. (If you have fairly large dates, like Medjools, use 2. If you have small dates, or an insane sweet tooth, use 3.) After the last date is incorporated, add the vanilla and a generous pinch of salt. (I've always loved the salted-caramel undertones that good blondies have.) Pulse several more times to distribute the vanilla and salt. Transfer the mixture into a single (unlined) muffin cup and use your fingers to pack it down tightly. (Or, you could just as easily form it into a cake shape on a small plate! Just be sure to press it together very  well so it doesn't fall apart.) Run a knife around the edge of the muffin cup and invert the blondie onto a small plate. Garnish with cacao nibs, if desired. (My chocolate-hazelnut ganache  would also make a perfect topping for this!) Notes Substitution Options - Nuts: any combination of nuts and seeds totaling \u00bd\u00a0cup. Choose from macnuts, cashews, pecans, or walnuts, as called for, or try Brazil nuts, hazelnuts, almonds, or even sunflower seeds. - Coconut palm sugar:  Sucanat, date sugar, maple sugar, unpacked brown sugar, evaporated cane juice, organic white sugar, or any other granulated sweetener in place of the coconut palm sugar. Or leave it out entirely for a sugar-free blondie! - Dates: 2 Tbsp of any sweet, soft  dried fruit instead of dates. \u00a0It would change the flavor a bit, but you could try raisins, golden raisins, prunes, dried figs,\u00a0or dried cherries, for example. 3.1 http://chefambershea.com/2011/01/22/the-5-minute-single-serving-raw-vegan-blondie/ \u00a9 2013 ChefAmberShea.com And that\u2019s it.  It\u2019s that simple, I swear! Eat it with a fork or simply out-of-hand, your choice. I\u2019m not trying to brag, but seriously\u2026this thing is outrageous. The oils released by the ground nuts combine with the succulent dates to make it astonishingly moist\u2026yet it\u2019s also nutty and slightly crumbly. The vanilla, sugar, and salt marry seamlessly into a butterscotch-like flavor. CRAZY, CRAZY GOOD. Not to mention: this blondie is fast, easy, and inexpensive to make; raw, vegan, and gluten-free; and unbelievably, mouthwateringly scrumptious. You have no reason NOT to make this! If you try it, please let me know how much you love it. Happy National Blondie Day, indeed! Check it out! Tara at Vegan Piggy  has already made my recipe \u2013 don\u2019t miss her post ! UPDATE: Alayna at Thyme Bombe  also made this \u2013 see her post  too! I\u2019m new to raw food.  Any idea what I did wrong? March 22, 2012  at 6:00 pm Amber Shea @Almost Vegan Sounds like you may have overprocessed the nuts.  If you blend them too long, they can release their oils and start to get kind of buttery.  Next time, try just pulsing them into coarse crumbs, and then pulsing the dates in until JUST incorporated.  It\u2019s ok if some big chunks remain.  Hope that helps! March 22, 2012  at 6:02 pm Hannah Ah!  You are right.  I processed the heck out of those nuts! October 29, 2013  at 2:44 pm Renee I made these, they were too dry. I used Bob\u2019s Red Mill chopped dates and coconut. What can I do add honey or agave do it will stick together? Thx. December 19, 2013  at 10:22 pm Chef Amber Shea Next time, use whole (pitted) dates, not the pre-chopped kind.  Pre-chopped dates are coated with flour to keep them in pieces, and not only will the flour absorb too much moisture, but the dates themselves will be too dry to contribute the needed stickiness. To salvage the ones you made, though, feel free to add a drizzle of honey, maple syrup, agave, etc. and process them again till they stick together. December 19, 2013  at 10:25 pm Renee Thank you, how much agave would you suggest? December 19, 2013  at 10:34 pm Chef Amber Shea I would add just a teaspoon or so at a time, then see \u2013 you can always add more if you need it. \ud83d\ude42 December 19, 2013  at 10:38 pm Carol These Vegan blondes are AMAZING\u2026\u2026only one problem,once I start eating them I can\u2019t stop.
